“You have zero chill,” Agatha mocked, amused.

“No, you have zero chill. You kept looking at me.”

“Did not.”

“Did yes.”

“Looked how? We were literally having dinner together, how could I not have looked at you…”

Rio’s smile got smugger, and one of her hands finally went to Agatha’s knee, index slowly trailing up her leg.

And now she was going to be the one catching fire.

Chapter 1: No Woman's Land

Heels clicking on the beige floor of the general surgery department, Agatha sipped on her coffee. It was a good morning. She’d had two full days of rest, which she’d spent taking Nicky on a day-trip on the closest lake and curling up on the sofa in front of a movie on his most recent obsession, which she kind of hated. Bugs. 

The morning meeting with plastics had been uneventful enough, residents from the previous shifts had managed to screw up slightly less than their usual, and there was no new complicated patient to worry about.

Such a good morning, it could only mean something bad was going to happen soon, something in the scale of mass disaster, hurricanes, earthquakes, a plane crash. 

She shrugged, stepping into the general surgery meeting room, and she was feeling so generous she even held the door open for the resident following after her like a stray cat.  She'd never admit it out loud, but she kinda liked this one. 

Well, tolerated.

Billy politely smiled at her, clutching his notepad against his chest as he slipped in. He waited for her to take a seat around the large square table taking half the room before sitting to her right. He knew better than to sit to her left, where, being left-handed, she liked to have a little more personal space.

Good boy.

She sipped on her coffee some more as Billy handed her some papers, charts of the patient they’d come to discuss. Oh, this was going to be fun.

As the general surgery team sat around the table, all known faces even though she couldn’t remember some (ok, most) names, she rapidly went over the chart.  That was when someone pulled back the chair to her left and decidedly sat in it.

And they were definitely too close, leaning towards her to stare at the big screen up on the wall. She turned back to shoot them a dirty look, whoever the idiot was. They all knew not to bother her by now, right? She had a reputation to uphold.

But, to her surprise, she actually hadn’t seen this idiot before. 

She was a young woman in her thirties, wavy dark hair and long lashes, her lips pursed as she sat back and glanced at her phone. When she noticed Agatha staring and looked up, her eyes were huge , and the warmest shade of brown.

Agatha’s frown deepened, and the woman’s eyes sparkled with something that looked an awful lot like amusement. And then she looked her up and down-an awful lot like she was checking her out...

"Have you heard of something called personal space?" Agatha bit at her, trying to keep her tone level. The girl-annoyingly so-seemed to hold back a chuckle.

"No one here knows what that is. Look around," she gestured at the room, cramped with attendings, nurses, fellows sitting too close to each other around the table, some residents to the back of their attendings, a student even standing against the wall.

Agatha was going to shoot back a reply when the chief of general surgery, a short bald man in his sixties, started introducing her, and she had to turn back to him, sitting right below the screen in his swivel chair. 

"Doctor Harkness, should your resident to introduce the case?"

Agatha barely nodded at Billy, and he sat up straighter as someone passed him the pointer. He opened the patient’s files on the big screen and started going over their history. 

"62-year-old female, obese with a BMI of 34, diabetes mellitus and chronic venous insufficiency. She got an hysterectomy at 45 and a gastric bypass at 50. No drug allergies… - 

Agatha shifted, highly aware of the woman to her left when she stretched her legs and her feet shuffled closer into Agatha’s personal space.

Ugh .

When she bent her legs back, her green scrubs pants slid up, revealing a pair of white socks with the word “BITCH” sewn into the front. Professional . 

Agatha turned her swivel chair more to the right, trying to get that annoying fuck out of her view completely. When Billy was done with the patient’s history and everyone started staring at her like she could snap her fingers and fix the case, Agatha stood up.

"Pictures," she pointed at the screen as she shot Billy a look, and he knew what to do. As she walked below the screen, a picture of the patient’s abdomen lit up on it. "Next," she said, and Billy complied. She slid a hand in the pocket of her white coat.

"Do you see this?" She pointed at the almost 20cm large necrotic wound on the patient’s abdomen as her eyes scanned the room. "You think slapping a flap on it will fix it?" a sarcastic smile started growing on her face, and she could see some weaker links starting to squirm. "Or do you think, maybe , you guys should try and manage the infection before we peel some more of her skin off to try and cover up this medical disaster?" 

No one replied and Agatha gestured at the screen for Billy, who went to the next picture.

"I have a suggestion," she continued, "look at this for all of five seconds and maybe next time you will light a few neurons before you call plastics for a procedure that only helps you get rid of a complicated patient for a few days. Mmh-kay?" She smiled wide, "We appreciate your effort."

She looked down at their chief, who looked almost as pissed at his colleagues as she’d felt at getting called in for the case. She shrugged apologetically, hands raising at her sides to gesture defeat . 

"But let’s make this a teaching moment, shall we? The resident who hands in the best plan of action for plastics on this patient-I wanna know graft or flap, how, where, when, blood supply, tension, everything-" she waved an index at the residents, " whichever of you does an acceptable job will scrub in with me when I finally cut…" she let it linger for a moment, "partially as first operator," and their faces shot up, " if  you general surgery guys ever manage to treat the wound." She crossed her fingers up next to her face as she made a toothed smile.

When her eyes fell on the annoying woman who’d been sitting to her left, her smile almost fell. As everyone else in the room looked away or frowned, she was smirking, eyes darker than before, and Agatha felt her control slip by the slightest of threads.

She turned back to the chief, patted his shoulder in a familiar gesture as she jokingly apologized about the situation, then strode out the room without a second thought.

And Billy, of course, was after her, perfectly timed as he handed her her half empty coffee cup.

 

***

 

"Did you see the new resident?" Billy asked as he skipped next to her along the corridors. They came to a halt in front of the elevators.

"What new resident? Isn’t it too late for interns this time of year?"

"You don’t know?"  Obviously she didn't know. Billy’s eyes widened to twice their size, mouth dropped open, but Agatha felt too nice today to tease him about it. "They transferred a resident from another hospital. She was sitting next to you…"

Agatha knew why his speech was dying out at the end of that sentence. 

"Oh, that one! Hmm, I hate her." Her tone dripped honey, but Billy knew better than to not take her seriously. They greeted some nurses as they entered an elevator, Carl… Coral? And, ugh, the other one was new. She’d have to ask for her name again; if they found out she didn’t remember, she’d never live it down. She’d have a month of endless venous catheters and blood tests on the nurses account.

"Why did they transfer her this late? Give me all the juicy details, Teen."

Billy’s cheeks reddened a little.

"Please don’t call me that…" He nervously looked around the elevator, even though no one could care less. Even less where Agatha was involved; she tended to have this effect when she walked around the hospital. People turned away and silently minded their business. Well, to be fair they were probably listening, but they'd learnt to hide it.

"And I don’t know why, no one knows. She’s a fifth year too, why transfer less than three months from the end of her residency program?" He raised his shoulders as they got off the elevator. "She’s the talk of the moment, but no one knows anything."

Fourth floor, Agatha’s favourite, and she felt her shoulders relax as they walked into white and lilac corridors. The place, other than the ORs, was basically her work-home. 

She let the topic Billy was yapping on about drop, switching to work as soon as they entered consulting room 14.

"Let’s get rid of these follow-up visits, we don’t even have that many today. We’ve got that kid with syndactyly this afternoon, yeah?" They both sat down behind the desk, and Billy nodded as he accessed his account on the pc and called in the first patient.

Agatha relaxed against her chair. It was going to be an easy day and she’d be home by eight, nine tops, she repeated as if it were a mantra.

She saw Billy in the distance scurrying over to the other residents, and of course he’d sit next to the new one, the golden retriever that he was.

The girl was basically lying on the table, head lying on crossed arms, but Billy didn’t take that as a hint to stay away, and he started animatedly gesticulating as he probably talked her EEG flat.

Hadn’t she been so annoying earlier, Agatha might have pitied her.

She had a point-Wanda’s pregnant belly was enormous, and watching her waddle around the hospital had become kind of comical. But the woman really loved her job. That, Agatha could respect.

Wanda patted her hand, smile too sweet.

"It’s ok Agatha, she just worries."

Mildly interesting: the new resident never sent anything. Suspicious: she’d seen them bending over screens together more than once. That was just perfect. 

"So, the flap is scheduled for tomorrow." said Wu, the chief resident, "as for today…" she went on to list which residents would be assigned to which attendings, and Agatha thanked the gods she’d exceptionally decided to grace the smelly changing room with her presence, cause now she got to have fun.

As Agatha strode away, already savoring the satisfaction of having that brat run after her all day long, she couldn’t help but overhear a resident whisper: “ The Purple Witch choose a new prey ”.

Her smile grew wider.
Let them talk.

Too bad smacking residents wasn't allowed.

And fine , the dressing was great, but it was too easy a job to mean anything.

Bitch-socks didn’t bulge. She smiled, seemingly enjoying the closeness. Annoying.

"Are you trying to get fired? What makes you think you can talk to your superior like that, bitch-socks?" and fuck , she shouldn’t have called her that. That exposed her. She wasn’t always good at keeping her temper level, and this brat was unhinged.

Ok, the praise might have made her feel a little more generous. Whatever.

"Don’t do that again."

Of course it would be interesting. Agatha smirked to herself.

"No, not that, don’t play dumb." Why would she mind people talking about her? She relished it, really. 

"Yeah, okay, sorry." Vidal pursed her lips and had the decency to actually look a little regretful. But then she smiled again. "… Bitch-socks?"

Fuck. It hadn't slipped her. 

Agatha had to turn away before she smacked that stupid smirk off Vidal's face and got herself fired.

"I don’t have a soft spot." it was a lie, she had Nicky, but this brat didn’t need to know. "What you saw is called bedside manners, but we’ve established you have an issue with manners, so, watch and learn."

And she strode into the next patient’s room, patting away the annoying thought that she had, maybe, regretfully, kind of enjoyed how unhinged Vidal had been. Agatha was a bitch-a powerful one, and she liked how, as busy and chaotic as hospitals could be, people always minded her and shrunk away from her path when she walked around wards. They respected her, they feared her.

By this time, maybe, she was in dire need of a challenge. 

She shook the thought off. This shithole must finally be getting to her head, cause no way in hell she’d tolerate-let alone enjoy-a resident standing up to her.

 

***

 

That night, as she went over the charts Vidal had updated before finally going home to Nicky, she felt a restlessness build up in her chest.

The charts were fucking flawless.




Chapter 2: The First Cut is the Deepest

Chapter Summary

Their first night shift together hehe

Chapter Notes

I don't even know. I'm sleepy. Hope this is at least a little fun. Probably some typos/mistakes here and there :P

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha yawned, barely remembering to cover her mouth, not doing it anyways. An on-call night after a day at her clinic really made her question her life choices. Why not abandon hospital life entirely? Energy-filled Agatha was an ambitious piece of shit, and she-tired Agatha-had to pay the price. Especially when she got called in for a big emergency.

The clinic was so organized and peaceful, and here…

 

The first responders barged in and set the rigid backboard with the patient down, a collar around his neck, as they rapidly introduced the case, people buzzing around and doing a million different things at once. 

“35-year-old male, high-speed head-on collision. He was ejected from the vehicle and found approximately 20 feet from the car,”

None of the trauma attendings were around, and Agatha frowned. Those fuckers. Wouldn’t be the first time they left a resident to fend for themselves. 

“Conscious but disoriented on arrival, GCS of 10,”

And the resident was, of course , because this was doomed to get worse, Vidal.

Well, at least she was a fifth year. She’d seen abandoned first years in similar situations before, and it hadn’t been pretty. Vidal might actually do something right. Or so she hoped.

And yeah, because Agatha had dared think positive, the residen was currently checking the airway patency, all the while making a mess of the patient’s facial lacerations and likely fractures in the process. Trauma surgeons were, simply put, classless butchers, and Vidal was clearly ready to become one.

“Vitals at the scene were BP 80/50, HR 130, RR 28, SpO2 88% on room air. We did 2 liters of saline and 2 units of O-neg,”

”Move. I’ll intubate, move on to the rest.” She didn’t even have time to make a snarky comment at how Vidal had been handling the patient’s face, which was just another of the downsides of emergencies. She physically stepped in next to her and Vidal slid away, easily letting her take control as she moved on to check the patient’s chest.

”Suspected tension pneumothorax, distended abdomen with guarding, multiple abrasions and contusions. No known medical history or allergies, no medications reported.”

As Agatha re-intubated the patient, because of course the tube had been misplaced by the twelve-year-old looking first responder, Vidal listened to the chest sounds with her stethoscope. Well, apparently a lack of sounds.

She asked for a chest drainage kit and Agatha stopped to look over her, just in case.

Without hesitating, Vidal made a small cut between two ribs at the mid-axillary line, to the patient’s left, to insert the chest tube.

She had good hands, Agatha found herself thinking as she went back to concentrating on her own job. And fuck, considering Vidal’s attending was nowhere to be seen (they would regret being alive once Agatha found them), it was also kind of her job to check on the resident.

At a first look, the patient seemed to have at least one open facial fracture, possibly more closed ones. The left maxilla, orbital wall, and nasal bones were exposed, but it was hard to see through the heavy bleeding—as heavily perfused as they were, faces tended to be messy.

And where were all the maxillofacial surgeons when they needed one? Night shifts, those fuckers all seemed to vanish.

And then of course , as Agatha worked on stopping the facial bleeding and Vidal did a quick neurological examination, the patient coded.

Agatha swore, not even trying to keep the volume down. No one would hear her either way. Machines were beeping, her compression on the facial bleeding was doing close to nothing to stop it—a major vessel had to be damaged—and Vidal was suddenly next to the patient, defibrillator paddles in her hands, forcing everyone to move away. Which was really bad for the gushing waterfall-no, bloodfall?-that the damned butchery of a face was.

She had to let it go.

 

”Clear!”

 

Vidal discharged once, a sharp jolt surging through the man's body, lifting him momentarily off the gurney before he collapsed back. 

The monitor line stayed flat.

 

“Again! Clear!”

 

Agatha writhed. She needed to find the source of that bleeding. Vidal shocked the patient again, he was still flat-lining, and Agatha couldn’t just watch anymore. 

She took the single step to her.

“Give it to me!” She practically tore the defibrillator paddles from her, Vidal so taken by the reanimation she took a second too long to react, and it was enough for Agatha to take over.

“Charge to three-sixty!”

“What the fuck is your problem?” Vidal practically screamed at her, “I know how to use a stupid defibrillator!”

“Dr. Harkness, it’s…” the nurse started protesting, but Agatha interrupted him.

”Do it!” The nurse complied, and Agatha pressed the pads against the guy’s chest. “Clear!”

They all stared in silence, even Vidal. The chaos from before had subsided like it had never even been there, time pausing as they waited for the monitor to show something . 

Each time this happened, those were some of the longest seconds in Agatha’s life. It felt like she could step away, grab a coffee and come back before anything happened. Come to think of it, it was almost relaxing, which was— maybe— a borderline psychotic thought.

 

The monitor beeped once, then again, a sinus rhythm setting its pace, and Agatha saw Vidal start breathing again in the corner of her eye. 

When she spared her a glance before going back to the patient’s face, she looked pissed, her eyes dark, but she was focusing on the patient nonetheless. 

Ignoring her, Agatha started packing the patient’s facial wounds to temporarily stop the bleeding before taking him to the OR, stabilizing the main fractures and covering up the exposed bones and tissues with saline-soaked gauze, all the while Vidal kept sending her the most annoying, distracting piercing stares, as if she were a cat whose tail Agatha had run over with her car.

At the fifth such glance, Agatha had caught up to her in terms of being pissed off.

 

When she was done and the patient was stable, she stood up from her stool, threw her latex gloves into the trash, and patiently, graciously waited a few seconds for Vidal to be done ordering imaging and an OR. Then, she unceremoniously grabbed her arm and pulled her towards the nearest on-call room, pushing her inside and closing the door.

“Ow, what do you want now?” Vidal rubbed at her arm, staring at her with big, mad eyes, shoulders hunched up.

“You were doing it right, ok? You didn’t do anything wrong. Stop looking at me like that.”
 “ I’m sorry I took over” , she could have said.
She didn’t.

Vidal seemed to relax nonetheless, shoulders dropping as she took a deep, shaky breath.

”Okay. Sorry I raised my voice, I guess.” She rubbed at her neck, and Agatha’s eyes fell to her fingers, now free from blue latex gloves. Yeah, she’d shown to have good hands in there, fast and steady. Good surgeon hands, and nothing else. Nothing about her thumb pressing into the side of her neck.

Agatha looked away. What the hell. Emergencies played weird tricks on her mind.

”It’s, you know, the adrenaline.” Vidal went on with her unnecessary explanations. Agatha just laid against the windowed wall between two bunk beds, looking up at her, arms crossed against her chest.

“You don’t need to apologize, I get it.”
 “ Maybe I deserved it anyways” . She wouldn’t say that out loud either.

Vidal nodded.

“I guess you’re not as bad as your attitude makes you look,” Agatha added, half rolling her eyes.

The resident's eyebrows scrunched, but Agatha could swear the corner of her lips was pulling up.

“Are compliments from you always back-handed?” Vidal stretched her neck against her flexing fingers, and Agatha had to keep herself from staring too long. She huffed to dissimulate any reaction.

“I don’t know what you mean.” she pushed herself off the wall, uncrossing her arms, and walked past her. “I need coffee.”

“Wait, aren’t we going to discuss the patient?”

Agatha opened the door and walked out.

“I still don’t know if you’re as bad as your attitude makes you look!” Vidal called after her and, forcing herself not to smile, Agatha finally turned around. The resident’s head was ridiculously peeking out the door. 

“Well, are you coming?” She gestured for her to follow, well-crafted unimpressed tone and facial expression slipping on. 

Vidal’s mouth turned into an “o”, eyebrows raised, and then she skipped after her as if completely forgetting the many “I want to burn you where you stand” stares she’d shot Agatha up until minutes before.

Well, she was weird. That much was clear.



***



“What are you having?” Agatha tapped her phone against the NFC symbol on the vending machine, and Vidal selected an overly sugared macchiato, because of course she would. Disgusting.

“Thanks,” she said as she took her cup and waited for Agatha to get her black coffee.

“Don’t even thank me, this shit is liquid poison.” She would have loved to get a decent coffee from the cafeteria, but they didn’t have enough time for that. They needed to get to the OR soon, by the time the nurses and anesthesiologist were halfway done with prepping the patient. But hey, feeding Vidal that shit was a sweet victory.

She spun to her, cup in hand.

“I’m going to give his face a temporary fix as you do the trauma part. Where’s your attending?”

Vidal shrugged as she sipped her coffee, a hand reflexively slipping around the phone in her pocket. “Home, I guess. Sleeping or… doing whatever the grown-ups are up to these days.”

She was so chill about it, chuckling and looking at her coily, Agatha narrowed her eyes. Something was up.

They started walking to the stairs, and she had to work hard not to spit out that acidic hell she was throwing down.

”Did you call them?”

When Vidal didn’t immediately respond, she looked at her to her left. She was checking the time on her watch, and immediately looked back up at Agatha, ridiculously long lashes batting over eyes heavy with sleepiness.  It usually hit hard right after an emergency, when the adrenaline subsided. 

It must be around 3am, but Agatha would rather not get confirmation.

“Oh, yeah. No, I didn’t call him.” She raised her eyebrows and grinned.

Agatha wanted to strangle her. She battled the need to scream at her right then and there. If she did it too often, it would lose its effectiveness, and she had a feeling this crazy bitch was going to make her wanna scream often as not.

She counted mentally, trying to level her temper, but only got to three before Vidal pulled lightly on her scrubs at the back of her ribs, making her shiver.

 

What the fuck?

 

“Where do you get the purple scrubs? It’s cool.” she pursed her lips, fingers grazing the fabric.

“Ooo-kay, first of all, don’t touch me,” Agatha spun around and batted her hand away, stopping in her tracks in between staircases, cause personal space, what the hell? And what the fuck was she even shivering about? 

“What? I thought we were besties. Y ou just grabbed me by the arm and dragged me around the ER in front of everyone.” She shrugged, a sly smile pulling at her lips. 

Agatha ignored her. “Second, you have to call your fucking attending. You’ve started working here, what, a week ago? We don’t know what you can take, and it’s a big case.”

Vidal didn’t shrink away, didn’t step back. She leaned even closer, and Agatha’s irritation peaked together with a warm sense of unsettlement, low in her stomach.

“Don’t worry Agatha , I can take it all.”

She was smirking, and the way her name sounded on her lips, so low it was almost whispered, made Agatha’s stomach flip. Frustrating, cause how dare she. S he basically growled in response.

“You will address me as Doctor Harkness.”

Fuck, she was maddening. And they’d have to spend hours in the same OR just now. Hopefully, getting her hands dirty would take her attention off Vidal, make her a little more bearable. 

She doubted it.

Vidal tilted her head like she’d just said something curious. 

”Right, as you prefer. You  can call me Rio.”

Looking disturbingly unfazed, she stepped back and waited for Agatha to start down the stairs again, following after her. At least that she always got right. The following.

And Agatha really needed a win. Now she wanted to break her.



*******



Very sadly, the surgery was so complicated that she didn’t have time to torture Vidal. It might also not be wise, considering the damned resident was elbow deep in the patient’s abdomen, removing his spleen and dealing with major vessels. 

She’d had nurse Espinosa phone the on-call trauma attending, and they’d said they were on their way. That , at least, had seemed to annoy Vidal. 

Watching her work now and then as she looked up from the guy’s face, Agatha found herself doubting the attending was going to be of much help, but of course, you never knew. Attendings were not just supposed to be there for the patient, but also to protect residents from making stupid mistakes that would change their lives forever. And yes, even this irritating brat was worth a few hours of her attending’s sleep. 

If he came and took over from Vidal, ruining the fun for her, well-that was just a bonus.

“Like what you’re seeing?” Vidal glanced up at her in the spare seconds she waited to get a clip, bloody hand relaxedly extended to the scrub nurse, and Agatha rolled her eyes.

“Just checking that you don’t murder the patient before your attending gets here, since I’m putting so much effort into making him able to breathe and eat in the near future. Emphasis on future- I kinda need him alive for that.” She gestured to Espinosa to pass her some gauze.

“Yeah, wouldn’t want to waste your time, right?”

“ Wow , this must be the first time we agree on something.” If she hadn’t had a mask on, Vidal would have seen her sarcastic grin. 

“Hmm, 'cause you’re one of the most expensive surgeons in the hospital, right? I'd better speed up.” Vidal chuckled, and Agatha wanted to choke her again.

“Answering that would definitely be a waste of time.” She smiled at her nurse, her tone light. 

As anyone but Vidal would have known, money talk in a room full of co-workers was a terrible idea, but apparently her lack of boundaries extended to depths unknown to mankind. Plus, no way she'd let Vidal give anyone here the impression she had any kind of power over her; surely it was already unsettling enough for everyone to have a resident not shrink before her in public. No spooking the babies.

Before the brat started talking to her again, Agatha asked a nurse to raise the music volume and started humming and singing along as she kept debriding a wound. 

Of course, the scrub nurses and Agatha had chosen the music. Of course, Vidal had tried -and failed- to add some songs of her choice. Eh .

 

******



Unfortunately for Agatha, the trauma attending hadn’t taken over from Vidal. He’d come, checked on her work for all of five seconds, approved every single detail of her management plan, and gone to take a nap with a “call me if you need me” and a wave of his hand. 

That had been bad for two reasons: one, Agatha hadn’t gotten her revenge on Vidal for pissing her off so much, and two: she’d had to witness her work for a couple more hours, and she was so good it had forced Agatha to feel some respect for her. Which was unacceptable and horrifying, seeing as she was an irritating little…

“Do you want to talk to the family?” Her voice cut through Agatha’s thoughts as she took off her purple surgical cap and crumpled it into her pocket, walking the corridors outside the ORs’ changing rooms.

“No, you will talk to the family. You can take everything, right?” She smirked at Vidal, and this time the resident didn’t smile. 

“Okay, I’ll do the talking.” She slipped her hands into her pockets, uncharacteristically looking at the floor in silence. 

What a welcome change. Agatha basked in the newfound peace, a relaxed smile on her lips.

They entered the waiting area for relatives and called for Mrs Larson; when she got up, a toddler in her arms and another kid following her, Agatha felt exhausted . 

Of course he’d be a father of two. Good for her she didn't have to be the one destroying their lives . Poor Vidal, huh.

 

They took them to one of the private rooms for meetings with relatives, had the wife- a light skinned, dark haired woman in her 30s- sit down across from them, then Agatha crossed her arms and looked at Vidal. The little girl in front of her was holding her mother’s coat so tight, Agatha couldn’t help but think of Nicky pulling at her clothes whenever he was nervous. She didn’t really wanna watch that.

“I’m sorry I had to take my daughters, I didn’t have anyone to…” the woman broke off, voice cracking.

”It’s alright,” said Agatha when Vidal looked down at the kids but didn’t reply. Weird. 

Then, Vidal started to explain: “Your husband is stable. As you know, he was in a car accident which caused major abdominal organs damage, but it’s under control, and we’re feeling positive about him pulling through this.”

The woman was clearly still terrified, but her eyes softened a touch, which in turn made her look more tired.

“He had severe spleen damage, which can cause profuse bleeding that’s a risk for his life, so we had to take his spleen out.”

The little girl looked worried out of her mind, but Vidal was just looking at her mother.

She went on to explain the rest of the issues, including rib fractures and the tension pneumothorax, and Agatha just knew that kid was hearing too much. When Vidal was done with everything but the patient’s face, the girl looked up at her, big brown eyes watery with oncoming tears.

“Is daddy going to be ok? He told me we're going to the park tomorrow.”

And Vidal stared at her, face blank. Agatha frowned.

A beat. 

Nothing.

She took over. “Doctor Vidal—Rio, is an incredible surgeon. I watched the whole time as she was taking care of your dad, and you can trust me: he’s so lucky to have her.“ she smiled at the kid, leaned forward and offered her a hand, which she took so fast it felt like she‘d been waiting for something to hold on to, even as her mother was hugging her shoulders to her side. 

“He won’t be able to go to the park for a while, but you can probably see him in a day or two, alright?” The patient was full of tubes and would be unconscious for a while; definitely not an experience for children. Agatha knew it personally.

“But Rio told my mommy that we can see my daddy now!” the kid was on the verge of tears, and Agatha ignored how intent Vidal’s look on her was.

“I’m sorry sweetie, your dad is very tired, he can only see your mom today. We need to let him rest, ok?” she let the kid squeeze her hand harder than such a small child should be able to; “can you do that for Rio and me, please?”

The kid pouted, small dark eyebrows knitting together, but after a few seconds she gave in.

“You promise I can see my daddy after he naps?”

Agatha nodded. “As soon as he can have visitors, you will be the first to know.”

She seemed satisfied by the answer and dropped her hand, so Agatha went on with explaining her plan for the patient’s face, trying to keep it as impossible to understand for a child as she could. 

Once they were done, she squeezed Mrs Larson’s shoulder as she weakly thanked them, and they went their separate ways. That had been a long family meeting, and there would be more. Many more. If everything went as hoped and he made it, the patient would have to adjust his lifestyle by a lot. For starters, he was already missing his spleen, and his face was not going to be the same.

 

Agatha shook the thoughts off; she needed a break. But first, she needed to take care of something. 

She turned to Vidal, who looked to be distractedly going towards the changing rooms, and grabbed her arm; Vidal turned to her, seemingly spooked by the interruption of whatever thoughts she’d been mulling over.

“Come outside?”

Her eyebrows furrowed, but she nodded so fast it was almost endearing. Or, wait, embarrassing. 

Funny how little she was talking now. 

They went out a door to an isolated alley that was used to transport stuff in and out the hospital, a place Agatha knew she could relax, and she laid against a wall. 

As Vidal untied the bun she’d made to fit her hair in the surgical cap, Agatha took her e-cig out of her scrubs pocket—she’d gotten it from the changing rooms as they’d passed through them as they left the ORs, and took a short puff. 

 

Vidal’s hair pooled softly around her shoulders; she messed it up by threading her fingers through her roots.

“You smoke? That’s…”

“Spare me.” She interrupted her, ”I’ve heard it all. Yeah, it’s terrible, and I’m a horrible influence on “the kids”,” she made air quotes with both hands, ”but at least I’ve switched to e-cig, and…”

“Have you read the research? E-cig is just as bad.”

Agatha took another puff and was really tempted to let the vapor out in Vidal’s face, but unlike her, she was a professional , so she didn’t. 

“Look, the day you find something that can help me let off some steam in this hellhole so I don’t end up taking out someone’s eyes, which in this case would probably be yours,” she’d taken a hand to the side of her mouth for that last past as if telling her a secret, then continued: “you can phone me.”

She smiled a big, sarcastic smile at her, and Vidal gazed intently into her eyes, thoughtful. It was kind of unsettling when she stared like that, but Agatha didn’t look away. 

Vidal uncrossed her arms then, a smirk pulling at her lips and making her look way less spent, and she took a half step too close to her. “I can think of a way or two, off the top of my head.” Her eyes sparkled. Agatha fought the urge to step away. 

Was she fucking flirting? With her superior? Who she didn’t know anything about?  

To be fair, she had kinda walked right into that one.

This time, she did blow the vapor in her face, but Vidal’s smile just grew as she raised an eyebrow. 

“Yeah? What ways?” She wanted Vidal to be the one to back down. As she said it, though, she might have been the tiniest bit afraid that the unhinged brat would actually step up and say it out loud. When Vidal had the nerve to slowly look her up and down, Agatha had this worryingly satisfying mental image of getting away, faaaar away from her after shoving her hard against the opposite wall. 

Shoving her against a wall. 

Her heartbeat picked up. 

Luckily, there either was a limit to her madness or she was feeling generous, because Vidal stepped away. She leant against the wall to Agatha’s left, smug smile still lingering. 

Fuck her, it felt like nothing could faze her.

Well, one thing could, but it wasn’t a fun one.

“What was that in the family meeting?” Agatha’s tone was more serious now, but she was still too aware of Vidal’s closeness to her side. She could practically feel the heat radiating from her arm, and the mere thought she noticed was utterly pathetic. 

Not like she hadn’t had little crushes in the hospital before, but—wait, crushes? No way, ugh . 

"What do you mean?" Vidal interrupted her thoughts, looking up at some random corner.

"You know what I mean. The kid."

"What about her?" She was totally feigning indifference, that light tone of voice and her eyes roaming. But she couldn't escape Agatha.

"Are you going to make me spell it out for you? You looked like you were scared that if you so much as acknowledged her presence, she would swell up and explode in your face."

Vidal took a deep breath and shifted.

" You told her I’m an amazing surgeon." She turned to Agatha and hid behind a smile again. Did she really think it would be that easy to slip away?

"Again, communication skills. She needed to hear that."

"Was it a lie then?" she pouted, and her eyes were so wide it kind of looked cute, and Agatha almost felt like patting her arm or giving her a hug, consequently wanting to climb to the seventh floor and jump off the building.

" Stop it . What was going on?" Her tone left no room for arguments; Vidal took another deep breath, she pursed her lips, and finally gathered the courage to stop playing.

"The kids shouldn’t have been there. It sucks that there was no one available to look over them as we talked to their mother."

Whiny . 

Agatha refrained from making fun of her in that specific moment, but it was so hard. She was being such a good person, she totally deserved a Nobel Peace Prize.

"But they were there. And that wasn't the best way to manage them."

Vidal crossed her arms on her chest but didn’t look away from her.

"Look, they hate us, Ag… Doctor Harkness." Agatha almost mourned the loss when she didn’t use her name. What the fuck was going on with her? "They’ll remember us forever as the surgeons who told them everything was going to change, and they’ll hate us. Or be scared of us, or both."

Before Agatha could answer, Vidal continued:

"I’ve tried before, it’s obviously not the first patient I have who has kids. The adults hate us, but they understand, most of them anyways, after a while. But the kids… There’s no way for them to wrap their heads around the fact they’re losing their father or mother or sister, or…"

Agatha’s fingers found her forearm, a gesture that came natural to her after years of comforting patients and their families. It felt a little different now, more vulnerable on her part, and it threw her off. She wished she hadn’t done that, not with that resident. 

Stupid habits betraying her.

Vidal’s arms twitched like she was going to uncross them and she’d changed her mind. But the back of her fingers was touching Agatha’s wrist now, and she didn’t move them away. 

Agatha pretended not to notice. 

She also pretended not to notice when her own thumb swept over Vidal’s forearm. 

The easiest part to not notice was how she wasn’t taking her hand back either. Of course, she was just doing this out of the kindness of her heart-no further motives. There was no pathetic tightening of her chest at Vidal’s fingers brushing her wrist, and certainly no compassion at her sad, deep brown eyes, which flickered down… to her lips?

Her eyes lingered for a few long seconds, until Agatha took her hand off her and leaned away. Her brain needed a factory reset, thank you very much.

"They could surprise you."

Vidal looked back up to her eyes, lost, until realization softened her eyebrows. 

"Yeah, well. They always can, I guess. People in general." She uncrossed her arms and rubbed her scalp. "That’s the magic, right?"

Agatha hummed, mind wandering over memories of her past work experiences.

"I guess I’m just tired," Vidal added.

Agatha looked at her for a spare second before answering, and she knew Vidal needed an excuse to hide away from what she’d said. So, the saint that she was, she provided.

"We say a lot of stuff after a night shift. Part of the fun, isn’t it?" 

"Oh, no," Vidal’s eyes opened wide and she smiled like a maniac, "the fun is having my arms covered in blood up to at least here," she showed her a point that was almost at her shoulder. Agatha snorted.

"Shut up, you trauma butcher."

They both laughed.

 

***

 

Vidal openly yawned in the face of her attending, not covering her mouth, and when he just looked surprised, Agatha rolled her eyes. That fucker wasn’t even gonna ask for a drop of respect. 

She went on briefing the day-shift team about the joint trauma-plastics case they’d had, making it as fast as possible so she could finally leave. 

When she was almost done, Vidal, who was rigorously sitting to her left as she enjoyed pissing her off even this late in the shift, leaned in to look at the labs on the papers in front of her. A subtle smell of shampoo or something caught Agatha's attention, Vidal's hair tickling her arm. 

She was so sleepy, her defenses so low, a thought seeped through her brain that the smell was kind of soothing. 

When Vidal touched her arm, Agatha’s head snapped to her-as fast as it could right now, which was not that fast—as she realized she’d gotten distracted and missed something.

"What?"

She sounded colder than intended, and Vidal's eyes widened slightly, a faint smile on her lips. She withdrew her hand. 

"Oops."

Everyone was watching them, but Agatha was too tired to verbalize the thought that they should close their mouths unless they wanted to eat some flies for breakfast.

"I meant: say again?"

"You forgot to mention the orbital fracture to Maxillo." Vidal was still leaning towards her, and Agatha hated it.

"What are you, a plastic surgeon now? Stick to your side. I was just getting there."

"Sure," she raised her hands up beside her face, palms out, definitely looking too smug and not too sorry. 

Agatha made a point to remark every single time Vidal missed a detail during her report, and by the time they were done, she was feeling positively avenged. So much so that when they walked out of the meeting room, she was overtaken by generosity.

"Breakfast before going home?" 

Vidal was so surprised she was asking, she actually glanced around to check if she was talking to someone else.

"Suure," she answered then, and Agatha caught the glimpse of a smile. Yeah, Vidal’s features were cute when she smiled. And god , she really needed to sleep, cause these intrusive thoughts were disgusting.

 

By the time they’d gotten to the cafeteria, Agatha couldn’t stand herself anymore. After she'd forced Vidal to order for herself, she just asked for a decaf black coffee, paid for everything and followed Vidal to a table, but didn’t sit down. 

"Why are you always paying? It’s unfair," the resident complained.

"Oh honey, what’s unfair is the amount of money you newborns get paid, and as you pointed out in a room full of personnel, I have it coming out of my ass." She shrugged as she waved a hand. "Don’t worry, you’re not special. I do this for the others, too." 

Vidal raised a smug eyebrow at her. Ok, maybe that last part had been flirting.
Actually, you know what? Not ok . 

"Not a newborn." She pointed to herself, "Almost 30." And why she felt the need to point that out, Agatha didn't know.

"Don’t care. All residents are babies."

"I’ll be an attending in less than three months." She mock-pouted. "Are you going to sit down? You’re creeping me out." But her lopsided grin said otherwise.

Agatha shrugged, then fake-smiled.

"No. See you never!"

She wiggled her fingers at Vidal and, basking in the confused look on her face, she walked away. 

Nicky would love it if she made it home in time to take him to school-rigorously driven by a driver, cause she wasn’t about to fall asleep on the wheel and kill her son. 

The thought of seeing his little face beam up at her warmed her chest. And just like that, she’d forgotten everything about the shift.

Well, almost everything.

Health workers' representation matters! ;P See u soon

Chapter 3: Winning a Battle, Losing the War

Chapter Summary

Agatha won't let Rio bully her-fuck nooo.

Chapter Notes

Keeping it dumb :P drama will eventually come

Agatha got two full days of rest. Doomed to be a zombie for at least the first 24h, she had to keep Nicky’s manny around. 
 And then, all too soon, it was hospital time again.

Two blissfully peaceful days, asking her 4-year-old son about his new school best friends, taking baths, reading, always made it hard to go back.
 Two full days of freedom from Jen saying things like: “I’m taking Vidal tomorrow”, and “ever thirsted after one of them?” as she tipped her chin towards the chirping residents.

God, life was good when Jen wasn’t withing earshot.

"What is this about?" Lilia mused over her lunch, and Agatha really didn’t care what Jen had to say. "Is this related to taking Vidal?" Lilia continued.

Agatha choked on her salad.

As Wanda patted her back, Jen snorted at her.

"About time you choked to death. And no, it’s not about Vidal, I just like the way she works. Unlike most residents, she makes my job easier."

"Who is it about then?"

"Answer my question first, Lilia."

The older doctor chuckled.

"It’s happened, yeah. We’re just human, right? Doesn’t necessarily mean we act on it."

"But did you? "Wanda beamed curiosity at her, and Lilia laughed. 

"Wouldn’t you like to know?"

"Not really, "said Agatha. No one listened. But she secretly did want to know, just a little.

"Something might have happened many years ago. I’d been an attending for a little over ten years, and this resident I tried to avoid just kept coming around. It happened, it was a little messy, but when I cut it off, he eventually got over it without too much fuss.” She shrugged, took a bite of her sandwich, “Now, Jen-” her tone left no space for argument.

And Jen leaned closer to the table, voice low.

"I think Wu has a crush on me. Is it bad if I enjoy it?"

She was smiling so bright–just her eyes, not her whole face, but it wasn’t lost on Agatha–and Agatha wanted to throw up.

"Yes, really bad," she answered fast, with a grin, earning a dirty look from Jen. Wanda turned to gawk over the surgical residents’ table, Jen slapped her wrist. 

“Don’t be that obvious!” she hissed, and Wanda jokingly slapped her back.
Should have slapped harder.

When Agatha shot them a glance, Alice Wu was sitting between Billy and Vidal, the latter laughing her ass off over something Agatha was sure was inappropriate at best, because Billy’s face was the color of a ripe tomato.

"Do any of the other residents ever flirt with you? "The words left her mouth without much thought, and Lilia eyed her suspiciously. 

But Lilia knew her audience. She was maybe the best judge of character Agatha had ever met; as such, she knew not to ask her too many questions, and she kept her doubts to herself.

"Not lately, "said Wanda, and Agatha laughed.

"Honey, you’re basically ten years pregnant. That might put most people off."

Wanda shrugged, a small fond smile down at her belly, rubbing a hand on it.

"I just have Alice making eyes at me over surgeries. "Jen’s eyes pierced Agatha, and she obviously wasn’t as people-reading smart as Lilia-"Why, who’s flirting with you ?"

Agatha immediately feigned the greatest possible indifference.

"Me? Do you know me at all? They’re scared shitless to even talk to me. How could they flirt? "She grinned, basked in the chuckles she’d prompted. 

She technically hadn’t said no–and Jen might not have noticed, but Lilia’s judging eyes roaming on her said otherwise.

"You’re horrible," Jen said, and Agatha giddily agreed. When Wanda joined Lilia in observing her for a few seconds after the exchange, she thought she hadn’t done too good a job at looking indifferent.

 

 

***



Later that day, she was idly puffing on her e-cig, wishing away the irritation from all the rich as fuck patients that had bugged her about minor inconveniences all afternoon. Five minutes of alone time wouldn’t be enough to recharge her, but she’d take what she could get. 

Another puff out, she crossed her legs and draped an arm over the back of the bench. Pulling strings to get a bench and a few plants on this roof had been the best of ideas-s he had many of those. 

She had closed her eyes, head falling back and basking in the sunlight, when a voice startled her. 

Her head shot up.

"Oh god, you ."

She was walking towards her, Vidal, phone in hand. She sat down next to her, clearly not taking the hint when Agatha spread her arm further along the bench to take more space, actually forcing her to remove it or else she’d be sitting against it.

"Happy to see you too." She sat down facing her, a leg bent on the bench, knee almost touching Agatha’s side. One hand encircled her own ankle.

"What do you want? This is plastics-my territory. Go away."

And she was dead serious, not even the hint of a joke in her voice, but the demon incarnate that was Vidal chuckled brightly.

"It's as much my territory as it is yours. Maybe more so."

"What?" That didn’t make any sense.

"Hmm." Vidal shrugged and laid her head against her hand, elbow on the back of the bench.

"O-kay, you’re just crazy. Nothing you say should be taken seriously, right?"

"Maybe. "she sang-songed.

Agatha didn’t look at her, but she knew she had one of those stupid smug smiles plastered on her stupid smug face. 

She kept puffing on her e-cig in silence, piercing holes into a vase as the resident shamelessly stared at her. She was certainly not giving up her favourite spot for her. Time for an evil plan to make Vidal leave.

But then, the resident finally stated her business.

"I checked on the trauma from the other night, thought you might want an update."

She unlocked her phone and handed it to Agatha, labs open on it. And well, that was kind of thoughtful of her-

Agatha went over the labs fast, only getting a general idea of the patient’s wellbeing: she was just interested in whether she’d be doing the reconstruction or not. Whether the guy was going to make it.

“Yeah. I also took pictures for you,” and she leaned in to open the pics on her phone as Agatha held it. 

There was that softly sweet, fresh smell again, and when her fingers accidentally brushed Agatha’s thumb over the screen, she withdrew from the touch by reflex.

She looked at the pictures, trying to ignore the tingling to her side where the resident was only inches away.

"Great. Also, you could have sent me all of this by text, did you know? Texts are these short messages that you can type on your phone and send to people who also have phones…"

And Agatha couldn’t believe she’d actually said that. She locked her mobile, let it dangle between two fingers as she slipped it in the scrub pocket over Vidal’s heart, and looked directly at her for the first time on that terrace. 

Her eyes, lighter than usual in the sunlight, were sparkling with mischief. Not amusing, fuck her very much. But-were her eyes actually hazel? Huh...

"You can ask my secretary for my number, as all the other good boys do."

Vidal didn’t answer right away, lips dropping half an inch open, and Agatha could swear her pupils were swallowing the brown center of her irises. 

And what the hell was that twist in her stomach?

She looked away, heart rate picking up a little. Crossing her arms protectively over her chest, she raised the e-cig to her lips.

"Can I get that? "Vidal pointed at it.

Agatha frowned at the rapid change in vibe. "What? Of course not." Crazy bitch. They were not a couple of friends sharing vapes.

"Come on, please? "she tilted her head, batted her lashes, and Agatha side-eyed her. That felt like one of her own moves–which was why it would never work on her.

"I thought you didn’t smoke."

"I don’t," She was beaming, hand out, palm up. "Come ooon."

Agatha rolled her eyes.

"Ugh, fine. If it makes you leave any faster." and she actually handed it to her. Which was crazy, yes. Maybe that move did work on her just a little-

Before she could feel fully disgusted at herself, Vidal stood up, slipped the e-cig in her pocket, and Agatha’s mouth dropped open as she started walking away.

"What the hell do you think you’re doing? "She was after her in two seconds, and in another she was blocking her way. 

But Vidal being Vidal, she was ok with physically walking into her, and Agatha had to move away in an attempt to keep a shred of professionalism.

"Are you fucking crazy?"

Vidal turned back to her, a big, unbearable smirk on her face.

"Game recognizes game."

"Give it back this second, or help me god I will ruin your life." She spun her around and tried to reach for the e-cig. Vidal pulled it away above her head.

"Tell you what, you give me your phone number yourself, I’ll give it right back."

Agatha was unsure whether to strangle her or push her off the side of the terrace.

"T ell you what , give it back right now, you don’t lose your job."

Vidal pursed her lips and looked up in fake thought, then she tapped her index finger to her chin, humming. "Hmmm, no. I think you're bluffing. You like me too much."

Agatha huffed. "That's never stopped me from getting what I wanted, darling." She wiggled the fingers of the hand she'd been holding out, realizing her mistake too late. "And I don't like you," she tried to correct, but Vidal was positively beaming. "If anything, I spend every moment you're close wondering if murdering you would be considered self-defense. I think it should."

Vidal wasn't impressed by her try at deflection, and only snorted lightly.

"You’re the funniest."

And Agatha was so done with not being taken seriously.
 Her chest burned in anger.

"Fine, whatever. Keep it as a souvenir for the day you're jobless and want to reminisce on the good old times. I'll just buy another." She shrugged, dipped her hands in her pockets, and with her shoulder hitting Vidal's as strong as she could, she walked back inside the hospital.

Fucking hell, she needed to get rid of that bitch.
