Needless to say, she couldn’t.

"Come on, Agatha, so she’s a little weird, don’t take our acceptable interns from us. "Jen rolled her eyes, Agatha’s frown deepened.

"Are you listening to me? She stole from me. The disrespect-"

"Why did you give her your e-cig in the first place? Sounds to me like she asked and you said yes."

“Sounds to me,” Agatha mock-imitated her, gesticulating, “You’re missing the point entirely!” 

Jen raised her eyebrows at her, and Agatha wanted to dig a hole in the ground and lie down forever. 

Better yet, Jen should.

"Agatha, do you like her? I haven’t seen you in such a frenzy over a coworker in-ever. And over such a small thing."

Agatha growled.

"I’m going to accidentally spill my coffee on your face."

Jen shrugged. "You’d do terribly in prison, bitch. No baths, no skincare, no luxuries…"

"I’m not you , Jen. I’d do great in prison. I’d be the queen of all bitches. Probably build a criminal empire. Have a lesbian army at my back."

Jen shot her an unimpressed look, but didn’t deny it.

"Don't you dare touch my face, Harkness."

The resident following Jen around that day, a short, blonde-haired guy, was very obviously trying not to look at Agatha as he patiently stood beside them in the break room.

Agatha growled again, free hand fisting at her side.

"Is everyone going mad? Ugh! "and she strode away. 

If she told that story, more people might question her relationship with Vidal. There was no relationship, there never would be, not in a million years, but fuck her if she was going to let them drill her on it, or believe something for even a second. 

The world was upside down, nothing made sense, and she just wanted to get through the day and go home.



***



Her next shift, Vidal was still there. Worse so, she was in her department, working with Jen. 

Knowing it beforehand hadn’t helped.

When she raised her eyes during the morning meeting, Vidal was staring at her, and she didn’t even look away after getting caught. She waved her hand and smiled like she knew it would piss her off. 

Agatha kept her stare icy, giving nothing back. No reaction was probably the best course of action, right? She just needed to ignore her.

Damn, at least she had Wu that day, which meant she might actually get to relax a little.

 

When the meeting was over, she tried to skip her usual coffee break with Jen, but the evil witch managed to drag her to the cafeteria with some lame excuses such as: “I want to consult you about a patient”. Jen would rather drown herself in mud than ask Agatha for her opinion when it wasn't strictly necessary: that’s how she knew it was actually about Wu. 

Jen wanted to take Wu to breakfast.

So, her “Sorry, I have a meeting with an important patient” didn’t stop Jen from physically dragging her as she protested that no one ever had those before 9am.

Whatever.

And Vidal just stood boredly next to Jen.

 

***

 

"Oh my god, really? "Alice Wu was looking at Jen, wide-eyed and smiling, as Jen went on with her story. 

Agatha wanted to roll her eyes out of her skull. 

She sipped her coffee and tried not to look over the table at Vidal, who–amazingly, thank god–was being as quiet as her.

"Agatha, do you remember? "Jen, from her right, interrupted her deep stare at that very interesting tree outside the window. Definitely more interesting than this conversation.

"What?"

"That guy! "Jen’s eyes sparkled with joy. Ugh .

"What guy? "Agatha’s tone couldn’t have been flatter. Jen huffed.

" Agatha , the snake guy."

Vidal, who’d been sitting back without engaging, only letting her eyes roam over Agatha as per usual, leant forward and rested her arms on the table. The movement caught Agatha’s attention, and when Vidal’s lips curved imperceptibly up at her, Agatha did roll her eyes.

"The guy who wanted us to make him look like a snake? "She glanced back at Jen, who nodded. "Yeah, that was kind of fun."

Jen frowned and slapped her arm. 

"What is up with you? You’re being so lame."

Agatha sipped on her coffee and looked from Jen to Vidal, who was studying her the way you’d watch a monkey in a zoo. Agatha hated zoos.

"Maybe I’ve lost my only means for winding down." She was obviously talking about her e-cig, and Vidal quirked an eyebrow as her smile deepened. 

Agatha turned to Jen. "Maybe I needed that before I used my brain power to listen to another one of your stories, Jen ."

Wu chuckled uncomfortably and shot Jen an apologetic look, and her fellow plastic surgeon was so distracted by that she didn’t even bite back a retort. 

Jesus-fucking-christ she was being a teenager.  That was a full-on crush.

As she pondered the depth of Jen’s fall into the abyss of pathetic thirsting, she suddenly felt a touch to her foot under the table, her head shooting to Vidal again. 

She just knew it had been her, and she knew it had been on purpose.

The resident shielded the side of her mouth from Alice and Jen as she silently mouthed something at Agatha, who, despite herself, leant forward.

"What? "She mouthed back, skeptical, and Vidal’s eyes and head gestured to the two surgeons sitting next to them, still deep in conversation. 

Agatha had to stare at her lips as she repeated what she’d said.

" They’re so obvious ," was what she understood Vidal was saying. She had a small gap between her incisors Agatha hadn’t really noticed before, and her lower lip looked fuller than she remembered…

"Agatha?"

Her head spun to Jen. Fuck, had she been staring?

"Yeah, Agatha , did you? "Vidal asked, and Agatha’s eyes narrowed at her, annoyance building up in her chest again. Correcting Vidal would draw attention to the use of her first name, so she didn’t. No other reason.

"Jen, look, as amazing as reminiscing about our enmity-development adventures is, I’ve got a lot of work to do today. Next time, you can schedule your…" Jen’s eyes widened threateningly, and she refrained from saying “dates” because she was too nice. Or because she liked having something hanging over Jen’s head in case she needed to blackmail her one of these days. "…Charity chats with residents outside my working hours. "

Jen sighed, trying to mask the relief as annoyance at Agatha, and Vidal chuckled. 

Agatha pushed her chair back then, she stood up and curled her index finger at Alice. "Come, chief resident. Let’s put your talents to better use." She laid a hand on Jen’s shoulder, "Sorry we have to cut this short, best friend !"

She turned and walked away, heels clicking softly against the hospital’s vinyl floors. Wu was quickly at her side.



***



So she couldn’t make Vidal’s life hell herself, true. But she was nothing if not resourceful, and she’d find other ways. 

Agatha tapped the pen against her desk in thought. She was in between patients, one had skipped their follow-up appointment, so she had a little time to think. Wu was diligently taking care of everything else for her, and she knew she could trust her. She’d still check on her work later, especially on the 3rd degree burns patient in pre-op, but for now she was fine.

She smirked to herself. An idea shaping into her mind, she got up, hooked the pen in her chest pocket, and walked out of her office. She was going to find Jen.

 

Talking to Jen was as simple as it could be (which meant utterly annoying, but uncharacteristically worth it). She had too many questions, of course, and knowing Agatha wouldn’t answer wasn’t enough to stop her from asking. But after all, she owed her more than one no-questions-asked (more like no-questions-answered, whatever). Agatha liked to stack favours.

That put her in a good mood, so she didn’t stop there: before having to go back to work, she called in a few more favors. She was going to have a blast.

All the gods graced her that morning by not having her meet Vidal more than twice, and both times they crossed paths, Vidal barely had time to look up at her. She didn’t smile her dumb grin at her, and Agatha’s wish for her to be having a terrible time seemed to be getting granted.

Nice. Agatha totally wasn’t missing the attention.

She went through the surgery that afternoon with Alice doing most of the work, Agatha just assisting her and the third operator, going in and out of the OR to take care of other patients. When she walked in the second time, hands washed and waiting for a nurse to dress her in a sterile surgical gown, she had to roll her eyes.
 But she was in such a nice mood, the scene only amused her.

" Jen , terrible seeing you here."

The fellow surgeon, who was standing behind Wu in her normal scrubs, careful not to touch her sterile gown, looked up from the surgical table to Agatha.

"Not as bad as seeing you, but you’re just who I was looking for." Jen chirped behind her mask, but didn’t leave her position. 

Agatha spun around as David, a nurse, held her surgical gown ties and then tied them for her. They handed her sterile gloves in that new brownish grey the hospital had acquired, and she swiftly put them on. The ritual was so familiar she could have done it in her sleep, without breaking sterility.

" Sure. "She smirked at Jen behind her mask. "What for?" She got to the table, a hand out for the nurse to hand her a small retractor, and looked at Alice’s work. She’d finished debridement and was now starting to harvest the graft, which was why Agatha had been called.

The surgery was pretty straightforward, a full-thickness skin graft from the patient’s groin to the anterior part of her thigh. She was a 30-something woman with an almost overwhelmingly sunny personality. She’d had a motorbike fall and the exhaust pipe had caused a deep burn to her right thigh, but luckily not much more damage. She’d get away with just a few scars. Big ones, yeah, but Agatha would make sure they were as pretty as possible, a work of art as per usual. 

She watched Wu work, instructing her here and there, as Jen went on about some patients Vidal was taking care of. Agatha knew what she was doing, using that as an exchange: Vidal was on the worst possible cases, and Agatha had to let Jen stay for as long as she wanted, or else she’d fuck that up.

Jen was being a horrible person. Agatha almost had to love her for that.

"Jen, do you know how horrible you are? "she smiled at her, eyes sparkling, and Jen raised her eyebrows.

"Right back at you."

"Yeah, but keep it up, you might be able to steal the crown. "

Jen scoffed, and Agatha continued: "It was obviously a joke. Don’t touch my stuff."

She stayed for a good fifteen minutes. Crazy how much time she could waste… but it was kind of fun to poke and prod her and see her wriggle in fear of Agatha saying too much, working her up until the point she finally left. Yeah, sometimes Jen was fun.



***

 

That evening, Agatha sat across from Wanda and Vision in a booth of the bar closest to the hospital. An emergency had led to her staying longer than expected, which meant Nicky would already be asleep by the time she got home. Might as well stay out a little.

Jen was sitting to her left, Lilia at the head of the table to her right. 

Agatha nursed her almost empty scotch glass, the alcohol already making her feel lightheaded.

When she tried to steal a fry from Wanda, she got her had patted away.

"Get your own! I need the extra calories."

"I don’t want my own, " Agatha whined, "They’re unhealthy."

"Then don’t eat hers ." Jen rolled her eyes at her, but Agatha couldn’t help but grin.

"I know why you’re not having fries. There’s something else you want to eat… or, someone ."

"Oh my god, Agatha, that makes it sound horrible!"

Jen widened her eyesin mock shock, the others laughed.

Vision was sitting with an arm wrapped around Wanda’s shoulders-they’d always been a cute couple.
 Agatha smiled at them, and, bleagh. Must be the alcohol making her sappy.

"This is so rare, all of us here at the same time." Lilia followed that statement by getting one of Wanda’s fries, to which the younger woman didn’t react. Agatha gaped at them.

"Jen, did you see that? Jen!"

"Shh, shut up!" Jen shushed her in a screamed whisper, a hand moving up to cover her mouth.

Agatha scraped the hand off her face.

" What ?" she whispered back. Jen’s head was half turned to the booth behind them, and everyone’s eyes focused there. 

" They’re talking about us!"

Right as she was asking, " Who?" Agatha tried to look to the other side of their booth, but Jen stopped her.

" The residents! I think they haven't noticed we're here!"

She held Agatha’s head down, and as much as Agatha wanted to slap her hands away, her ears trained on their voices, and she forgot about the rest.

"Yeah, her skin is so flawless it should be illegal!"

Billy’s voice. Jen hand-signed that they were talking about her, Agatha rolled her eyes.

"She does have incredible skin, yeah." Alice. "Billy, why do you like Dr. Harkness so much? She’s kind of scary. I mean-not to me..."

Liar. Agatha smirked at that, receiving an amused look from Lilia as Wanda and Vision tried to stop each other from laughing out loud like two idiots.

"That’s an understatement, he’s basically in love with her. "

Fucking hell. That voice, low and sultry, had to be Vidal’s. Agatha could picture Billy blushing hard at her comment.
Wait, sultry ? God. The alcohol, it was the alcohol.

"She’s a great teacher, okay? Haven’t you learnt so much from her?" Billy. Agatha found herself smiling fondly at the compliment, but when her view caught Lilia’s knowing look, she wiped the smile away, fast.

"Yeah, but Jen is so much more available… Rio, tell him he’s crazy!"

There was a pause, and Agatha’s heart inexplicably beat a little faster.

She heard a little chuckle then, her chuckle, and Vidal finally spoke:

"I mean, I do see the appeal in Dr. Harkness." Another pause. Hell. "Nothing better than topping someone that dominating." Agatha’s eyes narrowed as she tried to hide any reaction, carefully not looking at any of her friends’ faces. She swallowed hard. That unhinged brat.

"I can totally get why Billy is so in love…"

"It’s not like that! I’m gay! "Billy blurted out, causing both girls to laugh.

"Well, she’s hot . Maybe you… "

Agatha finally freed herself from Jen’s claws, her head popping over the booth as she turned and got up on her knees to be able to see to the other side of the backrest.

"Thanks, guys." She chirped, smiled wide at them, Billy turning impossibly red, impossibly fast, Alice choking on her beer, and Vidal…

She was sitting to the other side of the backrest across from Agatha, and she looked up at her, eyes gleaming in the low lights. 

"Next round on me for the free reviews!" Agatha continued, ignoring Jen’s hard slap to her arm.

She stared at Vidal, smirk mirroring hers: apparently, she had no shame. Well, Agatha had kinda figured that out already, but she’d still wished to catch her off guard…

She looked closer, eyes narrowing. Was that on her cheeks a blush? 

God.  She needed to see more of that.

She was about to tease her about it when Vidal raised her glass at her, and her drink looked exactly like what Agatha was having.
 Weird . It was the most expensive in the bar.

Agatha gave her one last, rapid glance before getting up and moving to the bar, pushing Lilia down when she tried to follow.

"I’ll get you another round too, Lil."

 

 

 

She leant against the bar, trying to push away that warmth in her lower abdomen that had settled there at the intensity of Vidal’s stupid eyes.

When a hand settled lightly on her back, she almost jumped.

Of course she’d see that as an invitation to follow her. Agatha mentally choked herself for being that stupid-Vidal’s closeness to her made the tingle on her skin impossible to ignore.

"Need any help?"

She turned around, and her dumb face was too close.

"I’m not taking the drinks myself. You know what table service is?" She sounded amused, definitely not as icy as she’d intended it to be, and Vidal chuckled.

"Are you always this nice to everyone?"

"No, darling. You get the extra package, no advertisements, 4K and all that."

She gestured for the barman when he looked towards her, and he signaled to wait.

"I'm a little disappointed you call everyone that." Vidal semi-whispered, her hand slipping away from her back as she sat on a stool to her left.

"Call them what?" Agatha shifted a little further from her, shooting a look to her booth. Wanda, that evil witch, was watching them. Under Agatha's stare, she smiled a little before looking away.

"“Darling”, “honey”. Kinda wish it were special."

She focused back on Vidal. That was some new level of crazy.
Her eyes were dark, long lashes batting slowly, and she did look a little flushed.

"How much have you been drinking?"

Vidal’s smile faltered a little. "Just the one drink. It’s been a long day, Jen had me do the most disgusting and annoying stuff for 12 hours straight… "

When Agatha smirked wide, Vidal frowned a little.

"Boo-hoo." She dried fake tears from her cheeks, "I thought you could take everything and nothing ever fazed you."

Vidal’s frown deepened. Then, realization dawned on her:

"It was you."

And Agatha shrugged, smiling wide.

"Did you really think you could play with me and win? Give back my e-cig, I’ll only keep this up for one month."

Vidal raised an eyebrow at her, looking mildly amused, but before she could answer, Agatha's index finger went under her chin, tilting her face up a little. Vidal froze, lips parted, and she sucked in a small, sharp breath.
Agatha felt her own chest flush.

"I do have a name just for you." She leant in a little. "Do you want to know?"

She could see Vidal hanging from her lips, and it was-wow. It felt good . She was so wrapped around her finger…

She nodded slowly, dark eyes shifting between Agatha’s. 

"You’re a little brat ." Her nail lightly scraped Vidal’s chin as she released her in a smooth motion.

Vidal took a few beats to recover, and how delicious that was.
Then the corner of her lips twitched, slowly shifting into a lopsided smile, her eyes searching Agatha’s face. She was definitely blushing now, and her pupils were definitely blown. As she leaned in an inch closer, her lips forming words, the bartender finally came, and Agatha felt fucking relieved. She didn’t want Vidal to get the chance to ruin her game.

She’d definitely won that battle.

Turned out Vidal had been having exactly the same drink as her, and when they went back to their booths, a bartender following soon, it also turned out Alice had drawn Jen and Wanda to her table. Agatha would have rolled her eyes, but as she sat down in front of Vision, she was in too good a mood to complain.

That was until Vidal sat down next to her.

"What are you…"

"You wanted your e-cig, right?"

Lilia smiled into her drink.

"Yeah, so what ?"

"Agatha, you smoke? I didn’t know." Vision and his polite voice.

"Yeah," she waved him off, "I would if this bitc- resident , weren’t crazy."

Vidal smirked. She dipped her hand in the inner pocket of her jacket and fished out none other than her beloved purple electronic cigarette.

"Give it…" Agatha tried to snatch it back, but Vidal leaned away, tricking her into leaning against her side. She huffed and sat back, arms crossed against her chest, as Lilia laughed at her.

"Harkness, I didn’t know you could be bullied this easily."

"Shut up." She was seconds away from acting crazy. Her fingers dug into her biceps.

"Did you know I played basketball?" Vidal absentmindedly threw the e-cig in the air and caught it back.

"Oh, you did?" Vision asked, sounding interested, and Vidal nodded cheerily at him. 

"Who cares?" Agatha’s fingers twitched. When Vidal raised her hand up and back, she got where she was going with that. And her instincts kicked in.

"Don’t you dare! "she all but shouted as she threw herself at Vidal, all pretense of professionalism gone, practically climbing on the booth to pull at Vidal’s arm that was holding the e-cig. 

Vidal tried to escape her clutch, Agatha’s fingers digging into her clothes and pulling on anything she could find as Vidal snaked away in every possible way. 

She didn’t register the gasps of excitement people sent their way as she managed to wrap an arm around the back of Vidal’s neck, the other hand shooting up to her precious e-cig that was being held up in the air…

Vidal’s head moved then, and Agatha felt her face, or something , against her collarbone through her shirt, and like a hundred bricks falling over her head, the situation dawned on her. 

She froze, hand in the air, the other clawing at Vidal’s jaw from her clutch around her head. Her body seemed to realize too then, and it got warm . Warm in all the worst places. 

When she met Lilia’s face, she could tell Lilia was trying (and failing miserably) not to laugh.

She hesitated a second too long. Vidal wriggled in her hold, and a sharp pain shot through Agatha’s hand. 

"Fuck! God!" She withdrew, setting the resident free. "Are you insane? You bit me! These are my only surgeon's hands!"

Vidal laughed like the maniac she was, pure joy in her eyes. She turned away, and the next thing Agatha saw was her e-cig drawing an arch in the air. 

Her mouth dropped open. It landed straight in the closest bin, several meters away. 

Agatha gaped, Lilia’s face mirroring hers, except she still looked amused.

Vision just hummed.

"Nice throw! But why did you…"

"Let it go, Vi. "Agatha wasn’t looking at him, barely able to pour the fake sweetness in her voice when all she wanted to do was scream. "She’s just signed up for months of the worst possible work in every single department she gets assigned to."

"But her residency is due in like two months, right? "Lilia mused. 

"Yeah, her being an attending won’t change anything." She turned to Vidal, "So, you either get a job in another hospital once your residency is over, or you’re mine. Every minute of your life in the hospital will belong to me. Either way, I win."

Before Vidal could answer, a dangerously smug look already on her face, Agatha pushed on her shoulder and motioned for her to get up. She got off the booth after her, rapidly said her goodbyes, and left. 

She didn’t turn around, but she could feel Vidal’s eyes on her the whole way out.

 

Once she’d stepped outside, she leant against a wall and took a deep breath. That bitch was simply unhinged. Hell, she’d been a little unhinged herself, but when the choice was between that and getting bullied…

Ugh , she hated Rio Vidal. Really, she did.

So why was her heart still hammering against her chest?

She closed her eyes and breathed in the cool air. Her Uber would be coming soon. Oh, how she needed her e-cig right now.

 


*** 

 

The next morning, she made a point of spending the little time she could with Nicky. She woke him up, coddling him when he refused to get out of bed. She knew he only did it when she was the one waking him, just a performance to get more attention from her, and so she gave it. When he hid under the covers, she played along to get him out, tickled him until he couldn’t breathe, then sat on his bed and held him until his breathing slowed, kissing his head as his little arms held tight onto her waist.

"I’m sorry I had to work so late yesterday, you know I always choose you when it’s even remotely possible, right?"

She felt Nicky nod into her arms.

"Mama? "He sounded uncertain, and Agatha leant away to look at his face.

"Yeah?"

"I saw a paper at school, Mrs. Day had it. It said that smoking is bad. "He paused, looking away from her for a second. "Do you smoke, mama?"

Agatha felt her heart clench. She took a few seconds to reply; she really hadn’t thought of facing the topic with him just yet. In the end, she wrapped her head around it, and-what a fucking coincidence, huh?

"No, I don’t." She moved his hair back from his forehead, but he didn’t look convinced.

"But you have that thing that makes smoke. I saw it at aunty Jen’s house."

Agatha raised her eyebrows in surprise.

"Ok, first of all, Jen isn’t your aunt. We hate her, remember?" Her tone was light, and Nicky chuckled. 

"We don’t hate her, mama! She makes me the best gifts! But-" he frowned, "uncle Vision too. And she’s pretty , and she told me the story about you and the snake…"

"Okay, okay, let’s not revisit that." Agatha playfully rolled her eyes. "Yes, that thing you saw is a type of cigarette, and it’s really bad, and I made a mistake. I promise I won’t use it anymore, okay?"

Nicky looked up at her, lips curving slowly upwards.

"Pinky promise?" he offered her a tiny pinky, which Agatha tangled with hers.

"Pinky promise. A friend of mama’s actually threw the cigarette away, so you don’t have to worry about it anymore. "

"He-she-" he paused, uncertain, "she did?" His face finally lost all semblance of doubt, a big smile cracking up. "Who? Aunty Jen? I bet it was aunty Lilia. You do everything she says, mama."

Agatha didn’t have to feign her shock at that. Mouth wide, she gaped at him. "How dare you! No one tells me what to do!" She tickled him again, and they laughed together. 

"Go get dressed now, before you’re late. I’ll make you breakfast."

Nicky pulled away, breathless, and smiled brightly up at her, an excited look on his face. He’d only recently started getting dressed by himself, even though she chose his clothes for him each night or morning, and every time Agatha was around to see it, he’d go and show off his work, proud. Agatha almost always had to fix something-an inside-out tee, or reversed shoes, but she made a point to compliment him each time in any case.

He ran off to grab his clothes from a chair close to his bed, and Agatha went downstairs to make him breakfast. Truth be told, she wasn’t that good at cooking-one couldn’t be perfect, and she was close, but there were a few things she’d managed to learn to make, for Nicky’s sake.

She thanked Nicky’s nanny, Josh, as she took over the pan he’d already-thankfully, cause they’d be late otherwise-been making pancakes in, and told him he could go home. He’d slept over, as he sometimes did when Agatha had to work late, and she was eternally grateful he existed. She paid him profusely, and it was worth every penny.

When Nicky finally came down, his little blue zip sweatshirt hanging wrong on him in every possible way, Agatha was setting two plates full of pancakes and blueberries on the kitchen island. She smiled at his proud, twinkly eyes, knelt in front of him and discreetly repositioned the sweatshirt, selling it as just a gesture of affection. It was funny, really, how many ways to wear clothes wrong he could find, but she’d learnt not to laugh at him too often.
She’d wait until his ego had built a little before teaching him self-irony.

"You’ve gotten way too good at this!" He smiled impossibly brighter; her heart melted.

She picked him up to settle him into a tall chair, and as they had breakfast together, Nicky telling her all about his recent drama at kindergarten, she knew she was happy.

 

 

That didn’t last long enough.

She dropped him off to school, letting go of his little hand as he ran to his friends, forgetting all about saying goodbye to her. She was okay with that. It was important for him to have a good relationship with school, even though it did sometimes make her a bit melancholic.

That wasn’t the issue.

She climbed into her car, laid her head against the headrest and closed her eyes. She hadn’t slept much the previous night. Not once, but twice, twice , she’d woken up from dreams of Rio fucking Vidal. Or, well, fucking Rio Vidal. The bitch had kissed her in her dreams, and she’d turned the brat around and bent her over the bed of an on-call room, and Vidal had loved it. 

Even thinking about it, the vividness of it, made her stomach coil and heart beat faster, warmth seeping into her face.

She growled. It wasn’t the first time she dreamt of fucking a coworker, that wasn’t the worst part. The worst, truth be told, was how Vidal had taken control in her dreams. She’d taken control, and Agatha had let her. Hell, she’d begged for it.

She took a steadying breath, irritation building up with the stupid arousal. She didn’t want Vidal. She hated her. The woman was a fucking menace.

Even as she told herself that, the picture of the resident smirking over her, knuckles deep inside her as Agatha's hands were tied over her head, seeped into her mind again-unwanted.

Fuck fucking Vidal. She needed to stop teasing her. 

She gave her overly expensive car a good kick before turning the engine on and driving away.

 

Chapter 4: Oh, the Guilt

Chapter Summary

When Wanda steals Billy's attention, guess who's left to help Agatha with her delicate case :P

Chapter Notes

There's a small Billy's POV, might be a pain for some of you, wish I could include links for you to skip it jajajaj but I don't know if that's possible?

Hope you enjoy! I kinda like the ending of this one.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

“Do you remember Ms. Doona?”

Billy offered her a coffee, which she gratefully snatched from his hands.

"The breast cancer patient?" He followed her closely, head tilted as he tried to hear her over the chaos of the ER.

"Yes. Her reconstruction surgery is scheduled for tomorrow, and I requested you to assist. I don’t want it messed up." She could see Billy nodding in the periphery of her vision as they strode to the elevators.

"Is that why you paged me? Is she already in the ward?"

Agatha didn’t hide a small, proud smile. Billy knew her workflow.

She nodded. "We’re going to see her now." 

She pressed the button to their floor, a hand automatically going into her white coat pocket to fish for her e-cig. It had been over two weeks since she’d stopped using it, yet the habit still popped up frequently. She couldn’t deny how much she missed it. She huffed, and Billy had the decency not to ask her about it.

They stopped by the break room on the plastics floor to finish their coffees, and Agatha was almost grateful for his rambling about his personal life. He’d started to date a nurse from their hospital and was trying to convince him not to move closer to his family in Chicago, or something like that.

Agatha smiled and made mock-interest comments at him, but, as always, they flew over his head. What a dork. He’d always been one to gossip and tell her about his personal life, but she had a feeling it had intensified since she’d caught the other residents and him talking about her in the bar. He was probably afraid she’d taken the teasing his colleagues had done seriously… which, come on, she wasn’t an idiot. Billy was a fanboy, sure, but she’d hardly ever met anyone gayer than him.

Vidal’s words, on the other hand…

She took her last sip of coffee and crumpled the paper cup a bit too forcefully, throwing it into the trash as she ignored whatever Billy was going on about, and walked out.

"Come, pet." She shot him a last look over her shoulder as he blushed and followed. Too damn easy to fluster.

When they walked into the patient’s room, Ms. Doona was sitting up in her bed, flipping through a tourist guide of some sort. She was a young woman in her late 30s, just a couple of years older than Agatha, of Korean descent. Her hair was short, halfway to her shoulders, which might have been related to the complete hair loss her chemo had caused.

It had been almost a year since then, and Agatha wished she could wait longer for the reconstruction, to let her tissues heal and check for recurrences of the cancer. Unfortunately, the woman couldn’t afford it, neither economically nor psychologically. So, here they were. They’d pay extra attention to every detail to make sure nothing went wrong.

"Hey Natalie!" Agatha smiled at her, taking her hand out of her pocket and squeezing her shoulder. "How are you feeling?"

The patient set the book down on her lap as she smiled up at them.
"Great, honestly. Remember I told you I was screwed because I’d left my job and everything?" She looked at Billy and grinned, "Sorry, language."

"Oh, don’t worry about it, he’s used to it. He works with me." Agatha gave Billy a little nudge with her elbow, but he didn’t dare confirm.

"Uh, it’s alright!" He smiled back at the patient.

"So, I thought: when life gives you lemons… I’m moving to Thailand, where I can live comfortably with my savings for months, and I’ll audition for jobs remotely. Not in a hurry to go back to work too soon anyways," and she laughed.

Billy chuckled, "Wish I could do the same."

"You wish you had cancer?" Agatha gaped at him, rapidly winking at Natalie, who was also sporting a shocked expression.

Billy folded as rapidly as a house of cards in a hurricane, blushing and stuttering that he didn’t mean it like that.

When the patient finally laughed, Agatha patted his shoulder.
"Agatha, don’t be mean to the resident who’s going to help open me up. I don’t want him to get revenge on my breasts."

Billy was–impossibly–even more uncomfortable after that.

"Alright, alright. Just because you’re my favorite patient." She turned to Billy, "Go on, tell me her history right, I promise I won’t bully you until the surgery is done." That was a blatant lie. She couldn’t resist teasing residents if she tried.

 

***

 

Billy yawned. He’d been there since 6 am, making sure everything was in order before Dr. Harkness’ reconstruction. It was only 7.30 and the patient, Ms. Doona, had just been brought downstairs to the ORs. He’d made the terrible mistake of going for one, one drink with Eddie the previous night, which had led to him only getting 5 hours of sleep. If Dr. Harkness picked up on it, she’d eat him alive, maybe rightfully so… but to be fair, seeing Eddie’s smile over his beer was worth it. All of it. Not such a terrible mistake. 

He could feel the smile take his full face, a fondness soothing over his worries.

Damn, he was down bad, and he was so ok with it. Especially now Eddie was thoroughly convinced not to leave for Chicago.

He yawned again. Thankfully, he had a few cards up his sleeve, he thought as he left the ORs to go to the cafeteria. He’d skipped his morning coffee in order to have it right before the surgery started, in hopes it would save him for a few hours.

He made his way through the hallways, rubbing at his eyes as he texted Eddie with one hand:

Billy: Cafeteria. Come save me before I flatline.

Eddie: Be there in 10. What are you dying from this time?

Billy: Just a lack of caffeine. Serious stuff

Eddie: Shit, that is serious.
Eddie: Don’t worry, it’s my field of experience 🖤

Billy chuckled, slipping his phone into his pocket as he stepped into the cafeteria. The warm scent of coffee and freshly toasted bagels wrapped around him like a hug, and he sighed. The line was mercifully short that early. 

He ordered a latte with oat milk, grateful for the personnel discount as always, and found a table near the window. The sky outside was still in that early-morning haze, not quite awake yet, but definitely more awake than he himself felt.

Eddie appeared a couple minutes later, tousled hair, sharp grin, a lazy confidence in the way he slid into the seat across from Billy. His own coffee in hand, black and fuming.

"Well, you look like death," he commented, taking a sip.

Billy huffed out an incredulous laugh. "You tempted me into the dark side last night. This is your fault."

Eddie smirked as his free hand went to wrap fingers with Billy’s over the table. "I’d say I’m sorry, but I’d be kind of lying."

Billy couldn’t stop the big, traitorous smile pulling at his lips, before launching into a description of what his day was going to be like. He knew he talked a lot, but Eddie seemed to be endeared by it... 

After a few minutes of much-needed normalcy, Billy checked the time and groaned. "Gotta get back."

"Try not to pass out mid-surgery," Eddie said, standing up with him.

"If I do, will you be there to catch me?" Billy shot back as they headed out, towards the stairs.

“Always.”

He blushed.

"Oh, fuck, not now!"

A voice, sharp and strained, broke through the quiet of the staircase. Was it…

Billy and Eddie turned in sync to see Dr. Maximoff, a super nice though occasionally terrifying neurosurgeon, halfway up the stairs, gripping the railing, wide-eyed and very pregnant, in dark blue scrubs.

Then he saw the wetness pooling at her feet.

"Oh, shit ," Eddie muttered.

Billy was already moving. "Dr. Maximoff, how do you feel? How long have you been having contractions?"

"Okay, let me help you," Billy said, slipping a steadying hand under her elbow. "Eddie, would you go grab a wheelchair from the ER?"

Eddie nodded and hurried away, leaving Billy with Dr. Maximoff, who was doing an impressive job of pretending she wasn’t in agony, face only twisting ever so little.

"Alright," Billy said, shifting so he was half-supporting her, half-guiding her down a few steps. He tried to sound steadier than he felt. "We need to get you down a floor so Eddie doesn’t have to carry you to the wheelchair."

She snorted between breaths. "Look, Eddie seems like a nice guy, but I doubt he could carry my very heavy twins and me anywhere right now."

Billy huffed a laugh, keeping his focus on getting her down safely. "Yeah, he’s not crazy fit. Definitely more than I am, though!” He wanted to keep talking, to take Dr. Maximoff’s mind off the pain. That was kinda his specialty. “Hey, maybe this was fate. You were just saying last week that I needed to get hands-on OB experience."

"This isn’t what I pictured," she huffed through gritted teeth.

"Yeah, I guess hospitals have a sick sense of humor. But you’ll be fine, Dr. Maximoff."

She shot him an apologetic smile, a little crouched, one hand below her belly like she was trying to hug the babies to her. “I think we’re past pleasantries. Just call me Wanda.” She smiled, but her eyebrows betrayed her worry.

Eddie crouched next to her. "Alright, let’s get you in before Billy decides to turn into a midwife."

Just as Billy was about to step away, one of the nurses turned to him, looking harried. “Dr. Kaplan, all our OB attendings are caught up in emergency C-sections and high-risk deliveries. Can you stay with her until we get someone?”

Eddie checked it and winced. “Damn. Trauma’s calling. I gotta go.” He clapped Billy’s shoulder. “Good luck with the babies, baby.”

Billy half-glared at him. He’d recently found himself incapable of really glaring at Eddie. “You’re leaving me? After that joke?”

Billy: Rio, get to OB. I need you, code red.

I’m supposed to be in plastics, and—”

He looked at Rio, who was watching the scene with scrunched eyebrows, hands in the pockets of her scrubs, and soon enough, he’d made up his mind. If his staying would make Dr. Maximoff feel safer, he would. This was why he’d gone into medicine: being there for people.

Aaand there it was.

She couldn’t think of anything to say, except-“Call it.” Voice ice-cold.

Vidal looked up at the clock as her eyes hardened, like claws digging into Agatha’s chest, because she knew exactly how she felt.
“Thirteen forty-two.”

Silence swallowed the room, the absence of the monitors’ frantic beeping fucking deafening, and Agatha was the first to step away.

Feeling on auto-pilot-feeling nothing, really—she pulled off her gloves with a sharp snap, not even stopping to stare at the blood staining her whole sterile scrubs as she tore that off too and threw everything into the closest bin. 

She didn’t look at the patient, she didn’t look at Vidal, she didn’t look at anyone. In a few, long strides, she was out.

 

***

 

Agatha rested her forehead against cool, wet yellow tiles, hot water streaming down her body. The parts of her that had been exposed—neck, face—had been stained all over with blood. She had to shower. She had to shower it all off, rinse and repeat. 

She drew another long breath in.

She’d been in there for a while when she’d heard someone—Vidal, in all likelihood—get into the other shower stall and turn the water on. 

What she hadn’t noticed until now, though, was the sniffling. Was it sniffling? Was she hallucinating?
She stood straighter, alert, ears trained to the sound. She must have imagined it, because…

Nope, there it was again. Someone was definitely crying. Someone she would ignore.

…Except she couldn’t. Because it was Vidal, and thinking back on it, she’d more or less blamed her when the emergency had first started. Maybe, maybe , she could have, like, not done that. Maybe she’d been too harsh.

Fuck.

Steadying herself, a steel plating to hide how soft, weak, and vulnerable she felt, she turned the water off, grabbed her towel from the hook right outside the shower and wrapped it around her body, tying it at the chest before stepping outside.

She paused for a moment. Maybe the showers weren’t the best place for serious talk.

But then she heard it again: a faint sob. And hell , she’d done way more embarrassing things than this.

“Vidal? Get out.” She leant on a hand against the wall, head dropped to stare at her flip-flopped feet. She felt so, so tired. But now wasn’t the moment for that. Now she’d think of the resident.

There was no response, but the sniffling paused. She wondered for a moment whether she should give up.

“...Rio, please. Get out.” She never pleaded. If Vidal didn’t come out now… 

Water sounds ceased and the shower door opened a crack, a hand coming out to grab her towel, and Agatha recognized it as the resident’s. At least she hadn’t gotten the wrong person.

After what felt like a month, Vidal finally came out, wet hair dripping water around her shoulders. And Agatha definitely wasn’t used to waiting, and Vidal wasn’t used to wringing out her hair before walking out of the shower.

She’d surely been crying, her cheeks flushed, eyes and lashes still wet—well, from the shower too—and Agatha couldn’t find it in herself to think of anything other than making it better. Even just a tiny bit.

Before she could say anything, Vidal’s brows knitted together by a sliver, eyes trained on Agatha’s face. Her lips parted slowly and trembled before she spoke:

“Did I do it?”

Agatha felt it in the back of her own eyes, burning, because she knew how Rio felt, and she knew it wasn’t her fault. She needed her to know that too.

“No.” Her hand moved of its own will to take Vidal’s, lifelessly hanging by her side while the other clutched at her towel. Vidal didn’t move at first. “It wasn’t your fault. Radiotherapy and surgeries had weakened the tissues, you know that. It wasn’t you, it was…” she had to swallow the next words down. “You didn’t do anything wrong.” She squeezed her hand, “You must know that.”

Vidal’s eyes searched hers, and Agatha didn’t waver. She had to make sure Vidal believed her. The resident’s wet eyelashes batted slowly, and she looked away. But she gripped Agatha’s hand back, hard.

“Okay.” Was all she said, almost a whisper, eyes fixed on something to Agatha’s back.

“I know you won’t believe me. Not right now anyways, not fully.” Agatha paused, thumb swiping up and down the back of Rio’s hand. “You’ll have the instinct to re-think of everything you did, over and over again, until every detail is burned irreversibly in your memory.” 

Vidal looked up, tears welling up in her eyes again, but before one slipped down her face, Agatha’s free hand went to catch it. The back of her fingers grazed Rio’s cheek and then she rapidly withdrew, burnt. The gesture had come unconsciously.

When Vidal’s head leaned towards her hand, though, her fingers stopped mid-air.

After a beat, even as her heart was aching from the pain, the shock, the fear, a thousand different feelings mixing up–she recollected herself, remembering her role. “Don’t. Don’t torture yourself. I promise it was not your fault.”  She cupped Vidal’s face, her cheek warm and soft under the swipe of her thumb. “I’ll be here if you need a reminder.”

Vidal’s eyes went back to her then, a flicker of surprise breaking through the exhaustion and the pain, quickly swallowed back. Then, she nodded. Almost imperceptibly. 

Agatha wanted to pull her into a hug, fuck the situation, to hell with how wrong it would be to hug a coworker in their towels, she just needed to fucking hold her. Hold her against her chest and show her how wrong she was if she still had a sliver of doubt. She needed to cradle her head and whisper everything would be fine. Even as she thought, to herself, that it wouldn’t. 

Rio clutched her hand a little harder before letting go, and Agatha’s fell back to her sides, fingers twitching. And then she watched her leave. 

She’d seen residents, attendings, nurses freak out before. Rarely, she’d held their hands and let them cry on her shoulder.

Why had it never felt this intense?

 

***

 

They got dressed in silence, separated by a line of lockers, and Agatha was aware of Vidal’s presence to the other side like it was prickling at her skin.
She was so tired, and it was just barely after lunchtime. And she didn’t feel hungry at all. What she really needed was a little bit of alone time, a safe place just for her to wind down. Hopefully, this hellhole would grant her ten minutes of isolation.

She closed her locker with a thud louder than necessary, and stalked away.

 

***

 

“Oh, fucking hell, Jesus Christ, no .” Agatha literally wanted to cry. Scream first, hit second, cry third. Not sadness-frustration.

Vidal just stood there, door clicking closed behind her, towering over her in a soft stance, definitely more recollected than before. 

Agatha was sitting on cement, her back against the wall, arms hugging her knees in the alley she’d made the mistake of taking Vidal once or twice. Her little, ugly safe place. She could see a piece of sky from there, and more importantly, no one could see her.

Vidal didn’t seem to take the hint, of course , as she stepped closer and sat down next to her.

“Would you leave me alone? In case you can’t tell by the swearing, I’m a little overwhelmed.” Agatha tried to use the last slither of her energy to burn her with a look , but Vidal just crossed her legs in front of her, hands wrapping around her ankles.

“Look, retract your spines, little porcupine. You took care of me, I just thought the mighty Harkness might secretly fall too. Besides, you always swear.” She shrugged tiredly.

“I… little porcup… what?” Agatha pinched the bridge of her nose between two fingers. “I used the last of my brain power to give you the pep talk, did my part, now just… trot off, go away. Run into the wilderness or whatever it is that you do when you’re not in my visual field.”

Vidal seemed to almost smile at that. Almost. And why did that make a thread of relief slither its way up Agatha’s chest?

“Do you do that with everyone?” 

“ What?” She bit back, exasperated.

“The… pep talk.” She made air quotes at that. “Do you always wipe away your colleagues’ tears in a shower towel?” Her voice was almost shy, almost uncertain, and Agatha was fucking baffled.

“No! What the actual…” She trailed off, “Does that seem important to you right now? Oh my god.”

Vidal shrugged again, hands twitching around her ankles. “I dunno. What’s important?”

“Uhm, I don’t know, maybe that a woman is dead? A patient I’d followed for months, who'd survived one of the worst, pieces of shit cancers she could get, who didn’t need that last surgery to survive?”

"Life is not about surviving-"

"Fuck that dropout flowerchild motivational quote," Agatha broke like a dam, and suddenly she couldn’t stop "Are you the one who chose to go through with it? No. Enjoy your last days hiding behind someone else's decisions or approval, when your hands are dripping blood from all the patients you killed, so many for you to even count, we'll see if you come to me with such a shitty-”

When she caught a glimpse of Vidal through her rambling, the resident was looking at her with a new expression. She hadn’t seen that on her yet. What was it, fucking compassion?

She certainly didn’t need her pity.

“The fuck are you looking at?” She barked, but it came out a tiny bit shaky, and Vidal’s glance drifted across her face. Agatha realized then: her vision was a little blurry.
Her cheeks felt wet.
She turned away from the resident, furiously wiping her face.

Vidal’s soft voice cut through her frustration. “Don’t do that. Don’t hide. My nanny used to say it’s harder to show our tears, but we’re stronger for it.”

When Agatha didn’t turn around, cause fuck whatever bullshit phylosophy that was, she felt Vidal shift next to her, until her hand brushed Agatha’s back.

“Can I?” Asking for permission to touch her-that was a first.

Agatha wanted to say no, to tell her to leave her alone, to push away. But Vidal’s fingers withdrew from her, and in a surge of panic, all she heard herself say was: “Whatever. Fine.”

Vidal’s arms wrapped around her and she pushed Agatha’s hands away from her face, pulling her into her neck. She smelled like shampoo and something softly sweet and earthy Agatha had come to recognize in the hallways, whenever she stepped too close. It soothed her. 

Her heart clenched. She didn’t deserve the soothing.

“Your nanny? I’m not five.” She muttered into Vidal’s neck. She surely didn’t feel five. No one had comforted her like this when she was five.

Vidal chuckled. “Are you sure? I could have sworn…”

“If I were five, you wouldn’t be talking to me. You’d be frozen, or running away.”

“Point taken.” a pause, then: “I’m only letting you win because you’re crying.”

Agatha wanted to teleport away. She wanted to dig a hole in the ground and put her head in it. Instead, she said: “Was she important to you?”
And she had no clue why she asked. She didn’t care about her coworkers’ personal life, not really. It was just a means to control them, but controlling residents was way too easy for her to put that extra effort.

Vidal’s fingers traced patterns against Agatha’s shoulder. “My nanny? Yeah, she was. She basically raised me—” Agatha hummed, but Vidal wasn’t done. “–After I was adopted.”

“Hmm.” She nodded against her, arms still clutching around her legs. 

“When I was six, thanks for asking.” Vidal’s voice was still soft, but Agatha could tell she was joking.

“I didn’t ask.”

“I know. Maybe that’s why I felt like telling you. Or maybe I'm distracting you to keep you from crying even harder. I'm nice that way…”

Agatha huffed lightly, and when Vidal tucked some hair behind her ear, she felt an overwhelming warmth take over. It was a simple gesture, but it felt so caring. And she needed to deflect.

“What about your parents? Where were they?”

“I don’t know, dead?” She joked.

“Rio. I mean your adoptive parents.” She almost had to roll her eyes. Vidal knew what she’d meant. She was teasing, and it was so familiar it almost felt like life could go back to normal.
Except she was breathing in the warmth of Vidal's neck.

“Hmm ,” she hummed, and Agatha felt the vibrations from her chest, “I like it when you say my name. You should use it more often.”

“Shut up.” It was so quiet and weak, like a little whine, it didn’t sound convincing at all. Just humiliating, really.

“Okay. You talk then.” 

When Agatha didn’t, Vidal finally answered: “My parents weren’t around that much. They were always working, planning something, they had events to attend. They needed me to be small and pretty and perfect, and that was kind of it.” Her nails trailed Agatha’s jaw, up and down, and it made sense, really, why Vidal was such a brat. 

She would have joked about how far she was from “small and pretty and perfect”, but she was feeling so spent, and so comfortable in a way, like coming home to her bed after a hard night shift… she let herself be quiet for once. Even as the guilt for it nagged at her chest. She didn't deserve it.

“I didn’t mind,” Vidal continued when she didn’t answer, “I had my nanny.”
Sure she didn’t .

“Do you still see her?” Agatha asked, and she found she did, in fact, care. She wanted to know. Anything was better than thinking about the present—that must be why.

Rio’s throat bobbed. “Oh. She’s dead.”

“Is anyone is this story alive? God . Did you want to make me more depressed than I already was?”
Aaand good job, Agatha. Always the most tactful, she was known for it.

But Vidal chuckled, and it was the best sound ever.
“I’m alive, aren’t I? My parents are, I just don’t see them that often.”

“Hmm.” Agatha considered keeping her mouth shut for a completely new reason. There was a pause, and her thoughts threatened to swirl again. She tried to concentrate on Vidal’s hands still soothing her, her arms still making her feel warm. The calm pulse in her neck compelled Agatha’s heart to slow down with it.

Right. She didn’t deserve to be soothed. She’d killed a person. Again. Because she always thought she could get away with anything.

“You’re not fit for this job. You already have blood on your hands.” Maybe her mother had been right. 

Just like that, a painful wave broke over her, and an unexpected, silent sob escaped her. She pushed to get away from Vidal, but her hold grew stronger, and she just ended up with the side of her face against the resident’s, Agatha’s hands now gripping the fabric over Rio’s shoulders.
Tears were probably running down her face again, she wasn’t sure. All she knew was that the world made no fucking sense, and she’d killed a woman, again.

Vidal pulled slightly back, their cheeks brushing, but her hands held Agatha’s head in place. 

“It will be alright.” she whispered into her ear, into her cheek, warm breath on the wet tracks left by her tears. “We’ll be okay. In time, it will get better.” 

She didn’t believe her for a second. 

“We?” Her voice raised from a whisper to angry, broken against Rio’s ear, Rio’s hands keeping her sane. “You didn’t make the choices, I—“ 

“Right. I know.”

She'd just done it again. Taking it out on her when she didn't deserve it. Fuck, she just couldn't do anything right-

"I'm sorry," it was a whisper, and it hurt like a bitch when it came out, but not as much as the guilt from making Vidal feel worse.

And her face was so close, her cheek so soft, Agatha’s heart hammered in her chest.

It hammered from the guilt, from the anger, the sorrow, from…

She shifted a little, face tipping to the side towards Rio’s, hands moving to grip the neckline of her scrubs of their own accord. Her pulse thrummed in her ears. It was too much, all these feelings, all the thousand fucking shades of hurt, and the–the yearning…

Vidal’s head tilted another degree, and her lips were just an inch from Agatha’s. She felt Vidal’s eyelashes flutter against her cheek and realized her eyelids, too, had been feeling heavier.

When Rio’s lips barely brushed hers, her chest caved in. Her stomach violently twisted, and she tipped her chin up. 

They kissed, soft and unmoving, and it tasted a little bit like salt. Agatha’s heart was in her fucking throat, and Vidal parted her lips. Her hands slipped around Vidal’s neck and into her hair, a little wet still, pulling her closer as the kiss slowly deepened, lips starting to glide. Before she knew it, Rio’s tongue, soft and warm, carefully traced her lower lip before Agatha granted her access to slide over her own, and the resident let out a breathy hum. 

Agatha burnt. Her breath hitched, their lips parted and found their way again, desperate, Vidal’s grip on the nape of her neck almost painful. For a moment, she didn’t have to think about anything else, heart racing and brain shutting down—or flaring up.

Then, as Agatha slowly sucked Rio’s lower lip into her mouth and drove her tongue over it, Rio let out the softer of moans.

And when it hit her—a deep, hot want in her lower abdomen—it was like a slap on the face.

What the fuck was she doing?

She pulled away, pushing Rio back, hands finding the ground to help her scramble to her feet. Vidal didn’t react at first, and when Agatha glanced at her she looked frozen in time, her hands still curling around the air where she’d been, wide eyes looking up, searching for her.

“What…” she managed, but Agatha was already walking away.

“Wait, Agatha,” she heard Rio struggle to get up, but she was already opening the door. “Agatha-”

And poof , she was gone.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 5: A Hard Day's Night

Chapter Summary

Messily navigating her grief, Agatha ends up finding out more about Rio's background.

Chapter Notes

Okie so I had food poisoning, couldn't write for a while :') that was fuuuuun.

This chapter is basically Agatha sulking and a little something else. Hihi

See the end of the chapter for more notes

When she heard back from Billy, Wanda had just given birth. 

Agatha managed to leave Jen to deal with emergencies, playing the dead patient card, cause she was nothing if not callous. Right? She hadn’t just recently cried in a resident’s arms. Nope. 

Denial looked good on her.

She didn’t knock before entering Wanda’s room. If she remembered correctly, Wanda would barely be conscious of anything other than her babies right now.

“Hey! Number one best aunt is here!” She announced herself. Vision, holding one twin to his chest next to Wanda's bed, looked up at her, tears in his eyes.

“Agatha.” Wanda smiled. She looked disheveled, tired like she’d run 12 marathons, but Agatha couldn’t help but marvel at how beautiful her ginger was right now. 

She walked up to her, briefly registering the tiny baby in her arms. “I’m so proud of you.”

Wanda beamed, then looked back down at her tiny human. “Who knew it would only take pushing out two babies for Agatha Harkness to finally tell me she liked me?” She chuckled. “I would have done it much sooner.” When Vision laughed, it sounded wet from crying.

“Come oon, you’re not Jen. You always knew I liked you, best friend .”

“I bet you call everyone that.”

Agatha shrugged. She felt happy for them, she really did. It didn’t mean she could just make the bitterness in the back of her throat disappear. One life ends, one—or two—begin, whatever the useless saying was. It didn’t make it feel any better when the blood that had just spilled was on her hands, again, because her god complex made her say yes to any surgery.

She took in the baby on Wanda’s chest better. It was as ugly as any, wrinkles and deformed head and all.
He was perfect.

“Do they have names?” 

“This is Tommy,” Vision answered, “And that’s Billy.”

Agatha nodded. So they’d called one after Wanda’s late brother. She released a deep breath, squeezing Wanda’s arm when a hint of sadness crossed her features. 

But the other twin…

“Wait, Billy? What the…”

“Do you not like it? It’s short for William.” Wanda shifted the baby in her arms and slowly, like it could break at a sudden movement, gestured for Agatha to take him.

“Is Teen the reason for this? Wanda, did he do something to you? Did his nerdiness put you under a spell when the birth hormones were making you vulnerable? Tell me, I will snap him in half like a twig.” She widened her eyes at Wanda, flashing a grin, and carefully took the baby from her arms. 

It was tiny, tinier than she remembered Nicholas ever being. Could be because he was a twin, could be she’d just forgotten how small they felt.
The idea of Nicky’s years slipping away through her fingers like that made an intense melancholy tie a knot around her throat. But the baby gurgled, stirring softly in his blanket, and Agatha’s chest melted. She smiled.

And then she remembered she wasn’t supposed to feel happy.

As Wanda was about to answer, the door to her room opened. Agatha turned around to the sound, and if she hadn’t been holding a literal, live baby, she would have dropped it and run.

“Hi, Doctor Harkness!” Billy chirped. “Look, look! They named him after me.” He pulled Rio by the arm, taking her to see Tommy.

“You have the wrong one,” Vision smiled, gently rocking his son. “That’s Billy.” He tilted his chin up towards Agatha.

When they got closer to her, Rio looked at her like a fucking wild deer. As if Agatha needed any more emotions to stir in her stomach, as if she didn’t have a thousand different ones competing already. The room started feeling suffocating.

“How did you get them to do this, Teen? What have you done? I’ve been working my way to it for years, you come in and steal the spotlight?” She was only partly joking, but Billy—the grown one—raised his hands in self-defense.

“I just helped Dr.Maximoff a little…”

“Stop being modest, you literally saved Billy.” Wanda dropped her head back against the pillows, tired.

“I mean, someone else would have done the maneuver if…”

Wanda cut him off with a weak wave of her hand and turned to Agatha. “Anyways, as much as we love you, I don’t think "Agatha" would be the best name for a baby boy.”

Vidal laughed. “Why not? It’s 2025. I dig that.” Head leaning down to baby Billy, she looked up from him to Agatha, and her face had gone back to almost normal, only hinting at a tiny bit of openness, like she was expecting something from her. 

And Agatha couldn’t bite back a retort when her claims had been supported. 

She felt unusually grateful at not having to think of something—the day had, and was, actively draining her.

“Well, there you go, Agatha. Rio will call her son like you, if she gets one.” Wanda mused, her eyes slowly moving between them, eyelids weighing down.

“Nah, I don’t want kids. Maybe Billy can do that, return the favour, full circle.” She grinned at him, and Agatha felt a pang of deception at her words.

With one last look, she put the baby down in his crib. She then proceeded to bark at everyone to let Wanda rest and found some lame ass excuse to go back to her department. That was definitely too many feelings for one, only 24h hours long, day… time to disassociate to make it through her shift.

 

***

 

A few days went by. Nicky insisted on meeting Wanda and Vision’s new twins, and Agatha had to wince through the happiness that kept warming her at seeing her son that excited. He didn’t seem to notice her mood, and she was always careful not to show, but kids could be way more receptive than adults, and Nicky would probably catch up sooner rather than later.
She really hoped later, because it was incredibly hard to resist him when he tried to make her feel better. And she wasn’t ready for that. 

The night after that first meeting for Nicholas and the twins, a Wednesday, Agatha had just thrown herself onto her bed, fully clothed but in comfortable sweatpants after reading Nicky a book to get him to sleep. 

She was going to fall asleep too, destroyed by the day of work and coming home to push through the tiredness to spend time with Nicky. He’d been particularly whiny today; he missed her. Not that they’d spent less time than usual together… Agatha suspected he might have started to feel her detachment: the way she’d been bottling her feelings was weighing down on him. She was used to losing patients, sure, but somehow she actually wasn’t, and as hard as she tried to avoid it, it always rubbed off on Nicky.

As her thoughts drifted off and melted into darkness, a bling startled her awake. She opened her eyes to see her phone light up, and as she thought of checking it, she slowly oozed off again. 

She wasn’t on-call, was she?

Another bling jolted her awake. She groaned, heavy arm moving to grab her phone.
When she saw who’d texted her, a small rush of adrenaline made her feel instantly awake.

 

Vidal💀 : Hey Ags, haven’t seen you in a while

Vidal💀 : I’m sad. Soooo, sooo sad. People always leave. Please don’t leave

 

As Agatha frowned, confused on so many levels it was hard to start deconstructing them, more texts came in:

 

Vidal💀 : She’ss druuuunk, ignore her–Alice!

Vidal💀 : Am not. Come over? We have drinks

 

That was followed by a series of random characters, like someone was fighting over the phone.

Agatha felt a pang of irritation.

 

“I have a 4yo son, I can’t just come over.” She typed.

 

She deleted that. No sharing info just because she was pissed.

 

Agatha: I have a life, I can’t just come over.

 

When she put the phone down, eyes closed again but still frowning, the tiniest sliver of guilt started nagging at the back of her mind. Ever since the… accident, she’d been avoiding Vidal. She’d seen her from afar sometimes, eating lunch in the cafeteria or walking around wards, and the times Vidal had spotted her, she’d looked like she wanted to reach out. 

Agatha had promptly bolted.

That was what she did. Run from anything that required emotional labor.

She’d promised to be there in case Vidal needed support after Ms. Doona had died, and then hadn’t kept her word. It wasn’t that she didn’t care, it just… maybe she cared too much. Maybe she’d been getting a little crush. Maybe she'd had several dreams about that kiss, in between dreams of her patients dying. Post-traumatic bonding or whatever.  

She couldn’t afford to care, she didn’t deserve it, and she certainly couldn’t open herself up to a fucking resident–least of all a crazy one she didn’t trust.

Still, she’d promised.

Her phone blinked again, and she held it up with resignation.

 

Vidal💀 : You’re right

Vidal💀 : I’m sorry

 

Her chest ached a little. Fine, she could talk to Vidal… maybe confronting one issue would make her feel a little more normal, a little more in control. She knew she wouldn’t be able to sleep now anyways, with all those thoughts swirling around her damned brain. Plus, tomorrow was a clinic day, she could survive one drink. She just had to call Nicky’s manny.

Truthfully, she knew she’d regret it in 12 hours, but the damage was already done.

 

Agatha: Where are you?

 

Vidal texted the address and a sticker of that guy from The Office going “Parkour!”, and Agatha rolled her eyes.

The fuck was she getting herself into?

 

Agatha: Call me Ags again, I'll burn down your house.

 

***

When she got to the address around an hour later, driven by her usual nightly driver, Agatha sighed. 

It looked like the fucking sorority parties they used to have in college.

The house, visible behind an open gate, was pretty big, with a nicely messy garden if not for the drunk people stumbling about. She’d expect them to be coworkers, but she recognized none of them as she looked between the overly diverse variety of trees and plants. 

She considered leaving, because this made it feel more like a drunken mistake than a drunken vulnerability text, but clearly she’d taken a second too long because, as she made up her mind, Alice came up to her window and knocked on it.

Now, the windows on this car were tinted, she couldn’t have known it was her. Still, the saint that she was, Agatha opened it for her.

“Oh, hey! Hi!” Alice chirped before seemingly realizing who she was and taking a step back from practically putting her head inside the car. Her excited smile only faltered by a tenth. “I didn’t know you were coming, Dr. Harkness. I was waiting for…” She turned around, distracted by a sound.

Agatha snapped her fingers at her. “Wu! I’m still here.”

She turned back to her and grinned. “Come, come! Rio is probably inside.” She stepped back and opened the car door for her, and Agatha rapidly instructed the driver to leave. She’d call him back soon. 

As she followed Alice inside, trying to ignore the unsettling feeling of Wu knowing exactly why she was there, Agatha kept looking around for familiar faces. All she found were a couple nurses and a guy from management— weird. Who were all those people?

Alice finally found Vidal in the kitchen, sitting on the marble counter, drink in her hand. She was wearing black slack pants and a cropped shirt that clung to her waist, neckline down to her stomach. Her hair was up in a bun over her head, her hands full of golden rings that matched the rest of her jewelry. And she looked so, so different than she did in the hospital, Agatha had to forcefully tear her eyes off her.

That was when she noticed the blonde, ripped guy who was pining over her as she grinned, and when she saw his hand on Vidal’s knee, an inexplicable, dark feeling twisted her stomach.

“Rio!” Alice carelessly pulled her friend off the counter by the arm, completely disregarding the guy. That made a subtle satisfaction pull at the corner of her lips.

Then, Vidal saw her. 

Her grin faltered, lips parting, and her brain must have short-circuited cause she blinked, pushed her glass to Agatha’s chest, and said: “Drink?”

Agatha raised an eyebrow at her. “Sure,” she went, a smirk slipping on to deflect from the discomfort of the situation, new environment and all, “if you can find another glass.” She pushed her hand away by the wrist, only trapping it between three fingers. 

Vidal looked down at the glass and back at her, then a little smile danced on her face.

“Why, I wouldn’t think you’d mind sharing bodily fl—”

“ Ookaaay,” Agatha interrupted her, clapping her hands together, “let’s get that other drink, shall we?” She didn’t look at Wu, but she really hoped she hadn’t picked up on Vidal’s terrible joke. Well, maybe her friend had told her everything anyways, and maybe Agatha’s career and promotion and reputation were already on the line.

Time to gather some info. Damage control.

“He already was in the ER. With her. Se te olvida ese pequeño detalle…”

“Yes, and he now claims he’s innocent, that you’re the abusive one, that you stalked and harassed him and her.”

Unlikely. Probably just family. 
Still, what if she were someone Rio still loved?

It was none of Agatha’s business, and she didn’t care. Shouldn’t care. The punch in the gut she felt at the idea had nothing to do with anything.

And yet, as Rio’s steps sounded towards the door, all Agatha could think about was finding out.

Had she imagined it?

She went after Rio.

***

Rio had already gone down a couple of stair flights when she walked into the stairwell; she was now standing in a corner at a landing, full body slumping against it. Weirdo.

Eww. Disgusting. She was going to throw up ten times, then pack her shit up and move to the other side of the world.

“Who wouldn’t?” She shrugged. “Give it a rest for a day or two, your lip is swelling,” she finally ended her previous sentence.

Rio silently rolled her eyes. Good girl, she learnt fast.

“Go get your heart broken in the OR now, Roberta.” And wiggling her fingers at her, basking in Rio’s groan and not one, but two raised middle fingers, Agatha watched her leave.

So much digging to do, ugh. The day was feeling more like a month.

When she got her, Wanda was just getting out of surgery. As Agatha walked by after checking on Jen’s OR for a consult, she saw Wanda rip off her surgical gown and throw it to the closest bin, and she didn’t waste the chance. 

“Hi-ya, neighbor! A word?” 

Wanda looked surprised, but she let Agatha’s hand on her back push her outside.

“You have an insane meal schedule.” Wanda checked her phone; Agatha knew it was around 5 pm. “Is this lunch?”

Agatha hummed. “I was having so much fun today, I forgot to eat until I started shaking. Look,” she held a hand out, Wanda inspecting it in what looked like genuine interest. “But let’s talk about you, sugar bums! “Tommy and Billy.”

“Just getting ahead, I can’t wait.” She shrugged.

“Alright, alright, I’ll tell you everything, okay?!”

The redhead chuckled, opened her eyes and sat up, and Agatha had to swallow a pretty big chunk of sandwich before she could keep going.

“We’re sleeping together.”

“I know.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “You’re the only person I’ve ever told, cut me some slack.” Maybe she was even a little excited about sharing.
Scratch that, no she wasn’t.

“You didn’t even choose to tell me…”

“Technicalities.” She waved a hand, “Here goes: no relationship stuff, it’s just sex, it’s fun, a lot of cardio, like, a lot—”
