“I said I’ll tell you everything, okay? So, a lot. Like a bunch of times a day cardio, and a bunch at night, and sometimes–”

“Now I know you’re lying, you don’t have all that free time. You’re always here…”

Agatha rolled her eyes through a smirk. She was exaggerating it for funsies, but, “Where do you think all that is happening?”

“Nooo, you’re doing it in the hospital? Agatha…” Wanda’s scolding tone was just going to rile her up. She should have known.

“Of course we are. We’re even making a list–”

“‘We’re making a list’ is not a good way to start a sentence about someone you don’t have a relationship with.”

Ugh, what did Wanda know? “We’re making a list of hospital spots to cross out…” 

“You guys are... Whose idea was it?”

“Hmm, I have to humbly admit it wasn’t mine.” 

Wanda looked at her in shock, but it was completely ruined by the smile that came through. “Just don’t do it in my department, okay? You guys are insane.”

“Sure, sure. Of course.” Well, now they had to do it in her department.

Wanda huffed out a chuckle. Then, “Are you sure it’s just sex? She punched a guy for you just today.”

Of course she’d ask that. Yes, she was sure. Rio apparently went around punching people for anyone, didn’t she? But Agatha couldn’t tell Wanda that; apparently she had some loyalty to stupid Vidal. And it wasn’t something she wanted to dwell on. ‘Cause what if Maya… No, stop it.

She shrugged. “I’m sure. Maybe we’re almost friends; she’d punch a guy for a friend. The woman is cray-cray.” Her eyes widened as she tapped a finger to her temple.

“And you aren’t? She matches your freak. That’s why I thought you might have something… more, together. I’ve never seen you fall in love, people get intimidated by you too easily. But Vidal... I think she could challenge you.”

She challenged her in bed, that was for sure. Challenged and lost. The rest, Agatha didn’t care about at all.
“Okay, first of all, ugh, I’m not falling in love with that psycho nerd. I don’t do, eww, love. Second, remember I have a son? And do you remember when you’d just popped your sons out, what did Rio say?” She didn’t give Wanda time to answer: rhetorical questions. “Third, she’s not the relationship type. Trust me, she’s too…”

“Fickle?”

Oh, so that was what Wanda thought of Rio. Not what Agatha had been about to say. “...Yeah.”

“I guess you know her better than I,” Wanda shrugged, “other than biblically.” Agatha hummed appreciatively at her joke. “You are aware, though, that she looks at you constantly?”

She was aware. Very aware. Wished other people wouldn’t notice. “I fail to see the point.”

“People pay you that much attention when they're into you.”

“She's into me enough. Biblically. Besides, take Kaplan: he looks at me, definitely doesn’t like me that way.” The simple thought made her feel like gagging.

Wanda hummed. “For the biggest ego I’ve seen, you’re really bad at admitting someone might like like you.”

“I’m not, because she doesn’t. She’s just playing around, as am I.” Agatha was going to die on that hill. That little voice in the back of her head that told her otherwise needed to be smothered to death.

“Oh. Well, that’s too bad. It would have been nice to see you fall in love, for once.” 

And just like that, Wanda let it go. Just one of the many reasons she wasn’t as annoying as Jen. 
But something was off…

“I’m good. There’s enough drama in my life as is.”

Wanda hummed, giving a quiet nod. Yet, something in her demeanor kept bugging Agatha…

And there it was: Carrot Head was not looking at her. She was not being sincere. She didn’t believe her, did she?
And why the hell would Wanda not believe her?
The voice in the back of her mind said Wanda was right.

The voice was stupid.



***



She had to survive through surgery next, only scrubbing in for the fun part: microsurgery on a torn tendon in a guy’s forearm. His wife had thrown a lamp at him, and they’d had to remove glass fragments for almost an hour; thank all the gods, fifth-year residents existed to take care of that part, and the opening and closing, because Agatha was just about to pass out.

All went well, and she was about to finally be done and leave, when Jen entered the OR.
Up to that, it was fine. Hi Agatha, hi Jen, sarcastic remarks, bla, bla. But then Jen had to go and ask about the band-aid on her neck. 

Fine. She could lie about the band-aid. All good. 

Then, as Agatha was trapped at the microscope, Jen had to go and lift the band-aid off her neck. And who the hell did that?

“It looks like a hickey,” Jen fucking said in the middle of the OR, putting the band-aid back.

“Your left eye will look like a hickey if you don’t leave right now,” Agatha very kindly offered.

She didn’t even have the energy to care what everyone else thought.

She sat on a bench in the changing rooms after that, tiredly taking off her surgical cap and letting her hair rain down her shoulders. If she didn’t go home soon, she was going to die right there, and they could turn her body into a nice hospital plant or something. 
Burying her face in her hands as her elbows dug into her knees, she sighed.

Someone walked in. Agatha had no will to look up. 

That someone walked up to her. Green clogs, green scrubs, white socks… Not just any white socks. She knew those socks.

A hand moved some locks of hair behind Agatha’s ear, and she didn’t hate it. 

“Bitch-socks, I’ve missed you.”

“Oh. Thanks.” Rio’s feet looked tentative. Could feet look tentative? Well, they did.

“Not you, I literally missed the socks.” Her voice lacked its usual bite. What the fuck of an answer was “thanks”, if Rio thought… Yeah, Rio didn’t like like her. 

The resident gave a small chuckle. Cute. Do it again.

“Come with me,” Rio said, and Agatha took a second before finally looking up. “I’ll take you home.”

And she didn’t need her to, but she wanted to go. She really, really wanted to get home, cuddle up with Nicky on the sofa, accidentally fall asleep… 

Rio offered her a hand, and for a second, as she stood up, Agatha dared to take it.

 

***

 

Slumped against the car seat, Agatha watched Rio’s side profile in the honey-tinted evening light. She only allowed herself to look for a moment, the warmth of Rio’s gesture sitting uncomfortably in her stomach. So unfamiliar, she wasn’t sure whether it felt scary or… 

Well, Rio had no business making her feel that way. So, in exchange for her act of compassion, she got several minutes of Agatha tiredly teasing her about her middle name. There were so many “R”s in there, how could she not point it out? 

Very disappointingly, Rio just gestured for her to get her wallet out of her pocket, proving the name wasn’t on her ID. Just a catholic confirmation name her nana had forced her to take, and given that she was not a believer, her sole religious devotion gone into making out with girls in Catholic school, Agatha technically had no business using the name.

Which obviously wouldn’t stop her.

By the time they made it to her place, both Rio and she had forgotten she wasn’t supposed to talk too much, and Rio was repeatedly trying not to laugh too hard, pressing her lips together to save the stitches.

When Rio finally parked the car, Agatha stayed slumped in her seat for a moment, so tired she didn’t feel like getting up. Was she supposed to thank Rio for driving her home? Sappy. Weird. No.

So she settled for: “I called you an Uber.”

Rio unbuckled her belt and pouted. “You’re not inviting me upstairs?”

On any other day, the pout would have worked. Agatha would have folded so fast, she wouldn’t even have realized until she had Rio in her bed. 

Today, though… ”No way, you’re not getting within a hundred meters of my apartment. You’re not allowed to have any of this,” and she waved her left index finger at herself.

“I know, just kidding,” Rio said quietly. “Wait, don’t move, this is super important—” And under Agatha’s confused stare, she got out of the car, rapidly circled it, and opened the opposite door.

Agatha stepped out and took the keys from her, Rio making a theatrical bow. 

“You’re an idiot,” she said, but Rio just grinned wider, and Agatha couldn’t help her own lips from curling up.

Ay, it was hard not to have Agatha and Rio kiss in every scene. Did I write them doing so? You can guess. One kissie in particular was painful to delete.

Chapter 11: Give a Little Bit

Chapter Summary

One more cute chapter. Don't get used to it ;P

Chapter Notes

Hi cutiepies

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The next day, Agatha woke up kinda annoyed. Because she’d dreamt of Rio again, as she hadn’t in a while, but this time, Rio had simply kissed her. Stupid Vidal had kissed her and she’d melted in her arms, and when she’d woken up in the middle of the night, her heart had been hammering in her chest. It had felt so real, like the very first time they’d kissed. It made zero sense. They’d fucked like bunnies over the past weeks, they’d definitely made out so much that there was no reason for Agatha to dream of that. Eww. She needed to get a fucking grip. 

Getting some distance back: that was what she needed. The sex ban had seemed like a terrible idea at first, when the words had slipped her–but it might play in her favor. Maybe getting used to Rio hadn’t been the most functional way to kill the crush. And well, she was Agatha fucking Harkness: she could do it. She’d make it out of the sex ban alive, looking as self-possessed as ever. She just needed a plan to survive the night at Rio’s… and she knew just how.

But first, she had to finally give Carol Walsh the meeting she’d been asking for, which was why she was currently, very much against her will, entering the designated meeting room.

Carol was on the phone when she got in without knocking. She never knocked with her, just to throw her off her feet a little. When Agatha gingerly sat down at an angle across from her, the Fox’s face twisted almost imperceptibly—Agatha had totally gotten to her—and she told whoever was on the phone that she’d call right back.

Good. That meant whatever this was wouldn’t be long.

“I’m glad you finally made it, Agatha,” Carol said with a cold smile. What she meant was: “no one has me waiting”, and for once, Agatha didn’t have to fake her cheerfulness:

“Of course.” She leaned back in her chair, elbows wide over the armrests. “What can I do for you?”

“Since I was in town, I thought of giving you some news in person.” She clasped her hands over the table, Agatha’s mind trying to anticipate her next words. The plastics chief was still months from retiring, couldn’t be that. Was she in trouble? Oh, bad news regarding her mother? She wished—“You’re getting an ASA medallion for surgical care advancement.”

Carol said that in a tone so casual, Agatha just stared at her for a couple of seconds before taking it in.

“What?!” was all she managed to answer, very casual herself. She would not smile like she cared, and so she frowned.

“You heard me. The ASPS nominated you.” Carol’s icy eyes didn’t waver.

“How would you know?” She wasn’t on the committe… and why the rush to tell her? Was it just a matter of ego, to swing her dick around about her connections? No, Carol wasn’t like that. She had her degree of vanity, sure, but she wouldn’t let it become a waste of her time.

“I have it on very good authority. Now, this is going to be good for the hospital—” oh, it was going to be fucking great. It would attract the best surgeons in the country to work there, and the wealthiest patients with them. “—So I need to ask: is there anything I should know that could jeopardize it?”

Agatha’s eyes narrowed in thought. Fuck, what the hell was she even talking about? Did she know anything? Did she know about Rio? 

“Nothing at all,” she said, as composed as possible.

Carol cocked her head ever so slightly. So fucking creepy to see it on her after getting used to Rio, still. “Anything about your most recent studies?”

Ah, great. She could breathe again: it wasn’t about Rio. Carol was just talking about Mrs. Doona, wasn’t she? “No one means to sue me or the hospital, if that’s what you’re asking.”

“Good.” Carol’s right index finger tapped the back of her left hand a couple of times, one of the rare involuntary gestures she hadn’t managed to get rid of. “I trust you’ll get everything else in order. After all, you’re the one who would benefit from this the most.”

Agatha unblinkingly stared back. Fuck, she needed to tell Nicky. He wouldn’t understand, but… oh, she needed to tell Rio. No, that was a stupid idea. She needed to keep it to herself until it actually happened, as she always did.

“Of course,” she cut through her own thoughts. “Is that all?” 

“That’s all,” Carol replied, but she didn’t move, and her index finger kept tapping.

Agatha stood up. If Carol needed more as the tapping was giving away, threatening to leave would pressure her to spill it. “Thank you,” she said, and turned away…

“Wait—” Carol stopped her, like clockwork.

Agatha had to school back the smirk from her face before turning around. “Yes?” Her voice held a little too much mirth. Oops.

The Fox looked different than usual, cold eyes slightly narrowed, brows mildly furrowed in a way that didn’t look like anger. She’d never seen that on her. Was it… worry? 

What she said next was the most surprising thing that had ever left her mouth. 

“Is my daughter doing well?” 

Agatha’s eyebrows shot up. Hands dipped in the pockets of her whitecoat, she shrugged. “I think she is.” And ffuuuuck, strike one. “I mean, we’re not close. Why are you asking me?” She should have led with that.

Carol also left her seat, standing tall in front of her. “You were involved in the… incident, yesterday.”

Oh, they weren’t acting like that had never happened? 

Carol’s chin tipped up before she carried on: “And I hold your people-reading skills in high regard. You have that something… just like me.”

She wanted to throw up. “I think you’re mixing up people-reading and manipulation,” she replied bitterly.

Carol didn’t even blink. “The two go hand in hand.” And shit, she wasn’t even wrong. Except, if you asked a good person, they’d disagree. Well, Agatha wasn’t good, no news there; but that didn’t mean she liked to be compared to Carol fucking Walsh. The next step would be a comparison to her own mother, and that… she’d do worse than throw up.

Carol stared at her for a moment before opening the door for her. “See you soon, Agatha,” she said curtly. And before she actually left, “Make sure everything about your latest clinical studies is airtight.”

And Agatha’s mind was so caught in swirling thoughts, she almost didn’t hear her. She was several feet away, Carol’s door closed behind her, when she processed it and realised: the Fox really cared about this. She could use her to get Sharon’s surgery, too.

She ran upstairs, threw the tank top over her bed–

 

Ding-dong!

Wait, Lilia? What?

Billy raised his hand. What the fuck?

 

“You, really?”

 

Billy cleared his throat. “I just wanted to say that I think you’re a great surgeon, and your parents don’t define you.”

 

“Great, thank you.” She looked around, trays hanging at her side. “Anyone else? Thoughts?”

 

From her back, someone snapped their fingers; Rio spun around—

 

“Me. I think you’re an asshole. Step off that table and clean it, people eat on it.”

 

Ah, there she was. She loved an entrance.

 

“Right. Sorry, Doctor Harkness.” She spun back around. “Meeting adjourned!” And she banged the trays together one last time. Damn, that was fun. She’d miss it.

 

When she looked down, the 50% bald guy was staring up at her with his mouth wide open.

She jumped down the table, dangerously close to Agatha, feeling smug.

 

“Just took your advice. Aren’t you proud?” She purred at her. 

 

Agatha looked utterly unimpressed. Damn. Without looking at it, she pointed at the table, standing her ground.

 

Rio gave her a small pout. And then, of course, she strolled to ask the kitchen staff for cleaning supplies.

 

Some interns and baby residents walked by as she sprayed alcohol on the table, and they slowed down next to it. She stared daggers at them, ready to push them away–

 

“We think you’re alright, by the way,” one of them blurted out. And then, clustered together like a bunch of baby chicks, they ran away.

 

Behind them, Agatha came to focus. She was sitting at a table, cheek resting on the palm of her hand. She smiled knowingly when she caught her eye, and motioned with her chin to her own phone on the table.

 

Rio fished out her phone from her pocket. She had a message from Agatha:

 

“You’re welcome.”

 

Oh, she’d scolded her in front of everyone on purpose. Rio’s chest warmed from it. Agatha cared for her. In her own way, she did. 

 

A few moments later, she was sliding back into her chair at the table with Billy and Alice, wishing so hard for Agatha to join them. She never would.

 

“That went well,” Alice said, “If anything, everyone who had been left out of the loop will know about you, now.”

 

“I’m a rip-off-the-band-aid kind of doctor.” Rio shrugged, resuming her eating. She picked up her phone as Billy started on one of his tangents about his patients.

 

She texted Agatha: “You haven’t told me how the reconstruction went,” and subtly sent glances at her as she nodded at Billy.

 

Agatha didn’t turn to her. Rio watched her side profile, face neutral, as she typed on her phone. 

 

Rio’s screen lit up–

 

Agatha Harkness: Come over tonight.

 

Was it her way of saying it went well? 

Rio chuckled at Billy’s joke, then looked back at her screen under the table. And fuck, she was feeling brave. 

 

Rio: For dinner?

 

Agatha looked up for a moment, fingers hovering over her screen. 

 

Fuck, say yes, Rio thought. Let me in.

 

When Agatha’s thumb finally typed back, it was just two letters.

 

Agatha Harkness: Ok

 

Rio’s grin took her whole face.




***




It was a slow day for Agatha at work, and she managed to get home pretty early. Rio, on the other hand, had all her boring resident work to do.

 

When she finally rang the doorbell, Nicky ran to the door.

 

“Mama, mama! Rio is here!”

 

“I know, munchkin.” She opened the door, Nicky jumping at Rio before she could even step inside. 

 

His arms went up and Rio picked him up, laughing a bubbly laugh, and let him hug her before putting him down.

 

“Hi buddy.”

 

“Rio, we made lasagna!” He took her hand and dragged her inside, to the kitchen. Agatha rolled her eyes. Still obsessed with her, huh. It wasn’t going away.

 

“Ooh, you guys made it?” Rio gave a smug grin, finally really looking at Agatha. “I thought you couldn’t cook.”

 

She huffed. “I can follow a recipe, okay? I just don’t want to.” She looked away as she set the food on the table, “The manny helped,” she admitted. Eh, whatever.

 

Rio helped Nicky into his seat, the table set. “We’re safe, then!” 

 

“You,” Agatha pointed a knife at her, purposely outside of Nicky’s vision field, “Won’t be safe much longer if you keep at it.”

 

“Just joking,” 

 

Rio’s right hand went to take the knife from her, fingers lingering over her wrist before she prided the metal away by the blade–Agatha’s skin tingled at the touch. 

 

“I’d very happily eat anything you offered.” Rio shrugged, looking directly at her for a moment before sitting down. “And I’m not just talking about fo—”

 

Agatha smacked the back of her head. “Not in front of him…”

 

“What, mama?” Nicky chirped.

 

“She’s making bad jokes. Now, eat.” And she slid some lasagna into his dish.

 

Nicky spent the whole dinner telling them about his day, about some drama between his kindergarten friends or whatever, and Rio smiled the entire time. She asked him questions, sounding genuinely interested, and offered her own stories in return. Agatha had to force filters on her—bit too early to tell Nicky the gruesome details, but other than that, she was… well, perfect. A bit too nice, if the stirring in Agatha’s chest was an indication. A bit too cute.

 

After playing around with him a bit, Rio insisted on cleaning up, so Agatha went to get Nicky ready for bed. It felt weird, having someone to rely on, even if it was just for one night. She wasn’t used to it. She’d always been a one-woman army—taking care of Nicky and herself, alone. Well, with Josh, but that was different.
She’d been alone even before Ralph had left, with him being unable to do anything other than be a second kid to take care of, ever since Nicky had been born…

 

“Mama, can Rio come listen to bedtime stories?” Nicky ripped her away from her thoughts.

 

She hummed. “If she feels like it. I’ll ask her.” 

 

Leaving Nicky in his room to play with a doll, she went to fetch Rio.

 

The resident was leaning back against the kitchen counter, phone in her hands, when Agatha found her. She’d cleaned everything up, loaded the dishwasher, probably put stuff in all the wrong places as she usually did when she was over—but right now, Agatha couldn’t care less.

 

“Hey,” she called her, pausing at the threshold.

 

Rio’s eyes shot up to her, a smile forming instantly, and she set her phone down. “Hey,” she replied. “Thought I’d give you some space.”

 

Agatha hummed, and she hesitated a moment before finally walking in. She stopped close to Rio, and once again, she wanted to thank her for the help, but she really fucking couldn’t bring herself to.

 

Her fingers curled around the hem of Rio’s green tee instead; the resident immediately pulled her closer, cool hands hugging her hips.

 

Fuck, it was soft. Wanda might be right. There was a little something there, at least on Agatha’s part. As Rio held her close, their hips and foreheads meeting, her heart thudded softly in her chest.

 

“We did it, by the way.” Her voice was low; she put a little distance between their faces to get a better view of Rio’s.

 

The resident just hummed a question, eyes shifting over her face. 

 

“Sharon’s surgery, it went great. We made it.” 

 

Rio’s smile widened, the gap between her teeth showing. “You made it.”

 

“Really? The one time I try to share the merit?”

 

“Oh, I’m sure the team members were all super helpful, but—”

 

“Idiot, I meant you. You and I. You helped make it happen.”

 

“Oh.” Rio swallowed. “We did it.”

 

“We did.” 

 

Rio’s hands traveled under her tee, up her naked back, bringing her closer. And she was about to kiss her, Rio fucking was. Agatha wanted nothing more than for Rio to kiss her, in that exact moment. Rio’s lips looked a shade darker in the warm light, so soft, but… 

 

“Nicky asked if you’d like to listen to his bedtime story,” Agatha cut off the moment. “You don’t have to, though.”

 

Rio’s face took a moment to react, eyebrows shooting up. “Oh. Sure, sure, I…” Agatha pushed both palms against the counter to get away, and Rio’s hands dropped from her waist. “I’d love to.”

 

You would? Agatha wanted to ask. She could not for the life of her fathom why Rio seemed to like hanging around Nicky. Her friends did it, fine, but this… they had a different deal. And it felt like something was shifting. And if it was all in her mind, Agatha would get burnt.

 

“Come, then.” 

 

As usual, she didn’t offer Rio her hand to take her with.

 

***

 

Nicky climbed on his bed. “Mama sit here and Rio here,” he patted to his left and right.

 

“Your bed is too small, we won’t fit.” Agatha helped him get under the light sheets.

 

“Can we get a bigger bed?”

 

“Yes, once you’re older.” She sat down at his feet. 

 

Rio was standing around, looking at one of Nicky’s books, studying the pictures.

 

“When?” Nicky asked,

 

“In a few years.”

 

“How many years? I’m almost five! Less than five years?”

 

Rio chuckled. “You ask a lot of questions. I’ll just sit on the ground,” and she sat down next to his bed, legs crossed. 

 

Nicky looked at her like she’d just said something curious. “Can I sleep on the ground?”

 

When Rio laughed, Agatha sent her a threatening look.

 

“No,” she said matter of factly. “Now, let’s–”

 

“Why not?” Nicky pouted.

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “It’s not as clean and soft as your bed. Come on, let’s read the book you chose,” and she held out a hand for Rio to give it to her, shifting to Nicky’s side.

 

They got through half of it—which wasn’t much—before Nicky fell asleep. Must have been an exciting day for him, wearing him out.

 

Rio was staring at her when Agatha stopped reading; face strangely serious, she kept looking for a moment before shifting to observing Nicky.

 

The kid was hugging Agatha’s side. His small hands twitched, then his legs. 

 

Rio smiled with her eyes. “He looks a lot like you when you’re asleep,” she whispered, and Agatha’s chest tightened softly. 

 

“You do that too,” Rio continued, her glowing eyes still fixed on Nicky’s face as she kneeled up to see him better.

 

“What?”

 

“Hypnic jerks.” Oh. The twitching limbs. “You do it every single time you fall asleep.”

 

Agatha just stared back. It was too soft, the way Rio was looking at Nicky, and the way she saw her in him, and—

 

“I’m out,” Agatha whispered. She carefully untangled herself from Nicky and stepped out, as fast but quietly as she could. She had to remove herself from… that. Because it made her feel like it could be something more, something she hadn’t dreamt of in many, many years. Something she’d never even believed she could have. 

 

Something Rio definitely wouldn’t give.

…Right?

 

“Hey, are you okay?” Rio walked up to her in the corridor, the door to Nicky’s room closed behind her. Her fingers were light on Agatha’s waist.

 

“You don’t have to monitor my mood, okay? I’m fine.” She snapped, keeping her voice low. When Rio’s face fell, guilt wrapped around her stomach.

 

“I wasn’t…” Rio’s eyebrows scrunched, “I’m sorry.” 

 

Fuck, classic Agatha. Always taking it out on the wrong person.

 

“No, no, I’m sorry.” She took a deep breath, cupping Rio’s face to take the frown away. “It’s nothing, I’m okay.”

 

Rio nodded, looking down at her lips, and Agatha was fucking drowning. 

 

“I need to shower–”

 

“Hmm, okay,” Rio cut her off, a small smile tugging at her lips, “I showered at work, so…”

 

“Oh. I see.” What? Her hands dropped from Rio’s face. She wasn’t jumping at the possibility to…

 

“I’m joking!” Rio chuckled softly, keeping her voice low. “I mean, I did shower, but—can I come with?”

 

“You’re not funny.” 

 

Rio’s tongue stuck out in a grin, and Agatha couldn’t help but smile. 

 

But if they were showering together, it meant she could now—

 

Rio suddenly kissed her, and Agatha’s breath hitched.

 

Fuck, fuck, fuck. It felt too good. Rio’s embrace made her melt, her chest warming with the sweetest sensation—she soon found herself pushed against the closest wall, but it wasn’t just hot. It was gentle, and everything she’d been trying so hard to avoid.

 

She pushed Rio back, the resident’s chest heaving as she looked at her in a trance. 

 

“Come,” Agatha took her hand.

 

***

 

She undressed her slowly, as Rio did her. One piece at a time, leaving a trail from her bedroom entrance to the attached bathroom. 

 

Rio smelled like body wash and warmth, and Agatha pulled her head back by the hair to mouth at her neck, careful not to suck a mark in such an exposed area.

 

Through Rio’s soft hums and hands roaming, they were in the shower, hot water on. She didn’t complain at her hair getting wet; she pulled Agatha in, kissing her under the gentle stream, wet lips gliding with no friction.

 

She may not be able to stay, she might never be more for Agatha—and for Nicky. But she’d just shown her something Agatha had never thought she’d see. It wasn’t for her, she’d always known as much. But to be shown a snippet of what couldn’t be—even though temporary, it was worth more than she could ever give Rio. 

 

When she kneeled for her, Rio’s darkened, heavy-lidded eyes went wide. 

 

***

 

Agatha kneeled, and if her heart hadn’t kept her standing by hammering against her chest, Rio would have fainted.

 

She looked up, Agatha, striking blue eyes and pointed nose, her lips red from all the kissing. So beautiful, as she’d painfully been all night as she’d shown Rio a part of her, the idea of eventually losing her hurt that much more. 

 

Rio’s thumb drew the length of Agatha’s cheek, and then she cupped it. She needed to hold on to her.

 

“Are you sure?” Her voice cracked.

 

Agatha didn’t answer. But her eyes, lashes wet with water droplets, didn’t waver.

 

***

 

Thank you, Agatha thought. 

And then, finally, her lips drank in Rio’s sweetness.

 

***




It was Sunday morning, and Rio had stayed over the previous night, after a couple drinks with Lilia, Alice and Jen. She’d pretended to go flirt with a random woman at the bar—Agatha had known it was just so she could use her as a fake explanation as to why she wasn’t driving home with Alice, but she’d still hated it.

 

“I was thinking about you the whole time I talked to her,” Rio had said as soon as she’d pushed her onto the bed, but Agatha had bitten her all the same. 

 

Rio was playing with Nicky in the living room the next morning, another rule broken. Those were starting to pile up.

 

As Agatha sat on the couch, a coffee mug in one hand and a book in the other, Nicky showed Rio all his plastic dinosaurs, one by one. They made up stories with them, and—embarassing as hell—Agatha didn’t manage to read a single page.

 

Rio smiled so brightly, cross-legged on the floor as Nicky stumbled around with his toys, Agatha couldn’t stop watching. When the resident caught her eye, she went right back to her book—totally stealth. Rio wouldn’t suspect a thing.

 

Of course Rio would be that cute with Nicky but not want kids. Of–fucking–course. Agatha had never asked her to elaborate on that; totally cringe, it wasn’t her place to question people’s life choices. Nothing to do with the fear of getting definitive confirmation that there was no chance, ever, for Rio to want to be a parent. Definitely not that. 

 

But what if… what if basing the conviction on one simple sentence from Rio had been too rushed?

 

What if Rio stayed, after her residency ended? What if she felt the same warmth in her cheeks Agatha did when they kissed—

And what if she could, eventually, want Nicky too?

 

Too many “what ifs”.

 

Rio’s plesiosaurus swam over Nicky’s arm to go munch on his face, and he giggled so loud Agatha completely melted.

 

Maybe she should ask Rio to elaborate. Maybe…

 

Ding-dong!

 

Her head snapped up to the door. Weird. She wasn’t expecting anyone. 

 

“Mama, someone else came over!” Nicky raised a dino over his head in exaltation. 

 

Looking more alert, Rio moved to get up, but as she went to the door, Agatha gestured at her to stay. Seeing as they were ringing directly at the front door, it was probably just one of her annoying neighbors. 

 

She swung the door right open—

 

“Hello, Agatha.”

 

Oh, fuck.



“I’m back for my son.”

 

***

 

The situation escalated pretty quickly.

 

When his father called for him, Nicky looked at Agatha for approval. She nodded with a comforting smile, and Nicky went to hug Ralph.

 

He ran right back to Rio, to curl in her lap.

 

Before things got heated, Agatha asked Rio to take Nicky to his room; she only turned to Ralph once Nicky was out of earshot.

 

“What do you want? You’ve been away for—“

 

“I know, Agatha. It’s not like I chose to. But I’ve been out of the psych ward for months, I’m better. And I want shared custody.”

 

Like hell she’d let Ralph take care of Nicky. Ralph couldn’t take care of an invasive plant, let alone a human being.

 

“No,” she said matter-of-factly.

 

Ralph huffed, a hand trailing through his hair. “No? He’s my son. You don’t trust me, but you trust that…” he gesticulated towards the corridor to the bedrooms, “what is she, your girlfriend? You’ve finally accepted you’re a dyke?” He spat out, keeping a low volume.

 

Agatha slapped his pointing finger down. “She’s not my girlfriend, she’s—no one.”

 

“Yeah, sure, if we go by your history, a no one you like to fuck!”

 

“Don’t talk about her that way,” Agatha scream-whispered. “And leave her out of this. Whoever I fuck is irrelevant, I’m still a fit parent. You, on the other hand, have never—”

 

“You don’t get to decide this, he’s my son too,“ he pushed past her, to Nicky’s room.

 

“What are you doing?!” Agatha was right after him, “You’ll give him false hopes, break his heart all over again!” 

 

Ralph huffed, waving a hand back at her. “I’m going to spend some time with my son, right now.”

 

Rio looked up at them from where she was sitting with Nicky; she booped his forehead and said goodbye, Nicky pouting up at her as she let Ralph take her spot.  

 

“Hey, little man,” Ralph had the decency to use a soothing tone, “I’ve missed you.”

 

And Nicky looked so confused, Agatha wanted to stab Ralph. Great, weeks of therapy rendered useless. 

 

She gave one look at Rio, and the resident followed her back into the living room.

 

“You better go.” Agatha crossed her arms defensively; Rio shouldn’t have been there to see all that. 

 

The resident hesitated. She looked back to the corridor, then pulled Agatha into a more private corner of the living room.

 

“Are you okay?” She whispered.

 

For a flicker of a moment, Agatha wished she could talk to her. What came out of her mouth instead, was—“Fuck, not this again. I’m fine, just go, okay?”

 

“I, uh–I just want to be here for you.” Rio’s touch on her arm, usually soothing, was making her nervous. She didn’t need anyone to comfort her.

 

“I don’t need you to be here, I said I’m fine.” 

 

“Agatha,” the way Rio looked at her, with fucking pity, was the worst. “I don’t know what’s happening, but—” she hesitated, “don’t keep Nicky away from his father. He needs–”

 

“You can’t tell me what my son needs.” He needed–what, his father? Certainly not. Agatha was enough; she’d had to be enough. “You think it was my plan to raise a child alone? You think I chose to? Fuck, god knows it was a terrible idea to have a son with a man I never should have married in the first place, but here we are. Nicky is the best thing I’ve ever made, however it happened, and no one, certainly not you, gets to tell me how to care for him. You’ve no idea what happened with Ralph—”

 

“I know.” Rio was looking regretful. “I know I don’t understand, because you’ve refused time and again to open up to me. I wasn’t trying to tell you how to be a parent, just—” She drew a hand through her own hair, “Agatha, just talk to me. Please.”

 

“No. You think I’m this nice person to try and help, but I’m not.” If Rio knew everything she’d done, she wouldn't even be there. “I don’t need your pity.”

 

“It’s not pity, Agatha, fuck, can you just let me care about you?”

 

“Care? You don’t know me. Stop pushing, you’ve managed to slither your way into my life, but it’s enough. Stay out of my business.” She took a step back-

 

Rio’s hands fisted at her sides. “Why won’t you trust me? I’ve told you everything. You know my worst secret, I-“

 

Agatha gave a sardonic laugh. “Hah, please, your worst secret is you fighting a little too hard to protect someone. That’s anti-hero behavior at best. I’m a villain, baby, and you know what villains don’t have?” Rio didn’t ask. She just stared daggers at her. “Nice little girlfriends giving them nice little pieces of advice,” Agatha concluded.

 

Rio flinched. She looked down; when her eyes got back to Agatha’s, they were dark, her jaw clenched.

 

“Great. You don’t have to worry about that, I never wanted to be your nice little girlfriend.” She spat it out like venom. “You make it sound awful.”

 

She strode to her backpack, pulled it on her shoulder and, under Agatha’s pointed stare, she left.

 

Still, as the door was about to slam closed, she had the thoughtfulness to stop it with a foot and slowly pull it the rest of the way. Probably still thinking of Nicky.

 

Fuck. Agatha was an idiot, but fuck Rio.
